(13th Central News Agency) (Changsha) The Hunan Provincial Government, based on reports from various counties of severe drought and soaring grain prices, considered the urgent need to provide relief for the people of the province. Yesterday's regular meeting decided on the following: (A) The Departments of Civil Affairs and Finance will dispatch personnel to investigate the amount of grain in each county. (B) The Provincial Bank will be ordered to purchase grain and rice for price stabilization purposes, with any profit or loss borne by the provincial treasury. (C) The Water Disaster Committee will be instructed to use existing funds to purchase and store grain. (D) County magistrates will be ordered to recall all released stored grain, devise methods to increase storage, and report the measures taken. Starting from August 11th, an export duty of one silver dollar per stone of rice and half for grain will be levied on export permits. The permits issued before this date will be reviewed and verified by officials dispatched by the provincial government. (13th Central News Agency) (Nanjing) He Jian telegraphed the National Relief Commission of the Executive Yuan, stating that most counties in Hunan Province had suffered from spring drought this year, delaying agricultural work. Since June, there had been no rain for consecutive months, and except for areas near lakes, there was a severe lack of water. A total of over fifty counties have successively reported drought disasters, and requests for relief from gentry and civilians have poured in. Besides dispatching personnel to investigate and submitting detailed reports separately, this telegram is sent in advance, earnestly requesting relief. Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi replied to the Hunan Provincial Government, stating that the severe drought in your province is deeply concerning. He has forwarded the matter to the Central Relief Commission to be included in the relief provinces and provide overall assistance. This is a special reply. (13th Daily Telegraph)

(13th Central News Agency) Ministry of Finance Prohibits

Import of Foreign Silver Coins 26

Foreign Silver Subsidiary Coins Are Not Included in This Exception (Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance issued an order to the customs superintendents of all ports, stating that the previous order from the Executive Yuan to prohibit the import of foreign silver coins in large quantities was already instructed to be followed by this Ministry's order on May 14th of the 19th year of the Republic. Later, a letter was received from the Consulate General in New York inquiring whether Mexican silver dollars (墨洋) were still legally applicable without restrictions in China. A letter was sent in reply that Mexican silver dollars were no longer allowed to be imported, and the prohibition had been communicated to all. Now, after investigation, foreign silver coins can be divided into two types: one is the commonly used silver coins on the market, such as Eagle dollars (Mexican silver dollars), Person dollars (Standing Liberty silver dollars), and Japanese dollars (Dragon coins); the other is silver subsidiary coins from other countries. Regarding the first type, the Eagle dollar was cast in Mexico for trade with the East, and the situation of the Person dollar is the same. The Japanese dollar is a currency that has been abolished in that country. None of them are legal tender commonly used in their own countries and should all be prohibited from import to uphold national dignity and purify the currency policy. As for the second type, silver subsidiary coins from other countries cannot be used in our country and are only carried by travelers. After arriving at the port, they are exchanged at small money shops, which has nothing to do with our country's currency policy and can be allowed to be imported. In addition to reporting this regulation to the Executive Yuan for record and issuing separate orders, it is hereby ordered that the superintendent instruct the customs officer to follow this order. (13th Daily Telegraph) Bank Savings

Should Be Divided Independently 27

(Nanjing) There is talk of amending the Savings Bank Law, but the Ministry of Finance believes that when ordinary banks concurrently operate savings bank business, they should be divided independently to protect the interests of savings depositors. Award-bearing savings are absolutely prohibited. How to handle the award-bearing savings that have already been conducted before the implementation of this law will be separately formulated by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. (13th Central News Agency)

Current Commentary

Nationalization of Silver Policy and the American Economic Crisis 28

Yesterday, foreign news reported that the U.S. government has announced the nationalization of silver policy. The content of the announcement generally stipulates that all silver existing in the market within the United States must be handed over to the mint within three months from August 9th onwards, with the official price set at US$0.501 per ounce (the official price for raw silver from mines remains at $0.645). Such a large purchase of silver by the United States has not only attracted worldwide attention but will also have a tremendous impact on countries like ours that use silver as the basis of payment. Therefore, we must first fundamentally understand the true nature of the U.S. silver policy before we can speculate on the effectiveness of the nationalization of silver policy. Since Roosevelt took office, the fundamental policy of the U.S. government has been to seek ways to restore the prosperity of the gold standard, which has already disappeared in the world. Therefore, in terms of monetary policy, it first abandoned the gold standard on April 20, 1933, on the one hand to avoid the collapse of domestic financial organizations and on the other hand to intensify the United States' offensive in the world market. When the ambitions of the major countries participating in the London Conference were fully exposed last July, Roosevelt, witnessing that the world crisis could still not be eliminated, decided to adopt a two-pronged approach, setting a thorough policy of concentrating cash and inflating the currency. The gold purchase movement in late October last year, the silver purchase bill in May this year, and the recent nationalization of silver law are all based on this consistent spirit. The practical significance of so-called currency inflation is nothing more than giving a discount to labor costs on the one hand and raising the competitive strength of American goods in the international market on the other hand. Originally, after the price of silver rose, first, the silver-using countries' market could experience a temporary increase in purchasing power, and second, the exchange rate of the U.S. dollar would tend to fall when the nationalization of silver was announced and large-scale foreign silver purchases were carried out. These are all important steps in Roosevelt's (optimistically successful) monetary policy.

What will be the reaction of other industrial countries to the U.S. silver policy? During the period of several evolutions of the U.S. monetary policy in the past year or so, Britain's Exchange Equalisation Account has increased by £200 million, and its active integration of the Sterling Area is no less than an important tool to help it carry out the exchange rate war. As for the European Gold Bloc countries under the leadership of France, their national fiscal austerity plans, as well as plans to reduce wages, interest rates, and rents, are another form of group to counter the U.S. monetary policy. Now that the United States has decided to carry out a large-scale silver purchase method, on the one hand, it is no less than explaining that the purpose of its past gold purchase movement has not been fully realized, and at the same time, it also points out that it has begun to wage a more acute market war against industrial countries such as Britain, France, Germany, Italy, and Japan. However, such a heated market war can only intensify world panic, and the question of how to raise purchasing power remains unresolved.

The above has already stated that the basic purpose of the U.S. silver policy is to restore the country's already vanished prosperity. Roosevelt's policies in the past year or so have taken this as their starting point. However, what is the effect? You can understand by looking at the recent months of surging labor strikes in the United States. We can now see from the law on the return of silver to national ownership that Roosevelt is still unwilling to abandon his past policies. Although we dare not say that this is a (last-gasp) phenomenon, we can only admit that it is a powerful tonic.

Stalemate in Sino-Soviet Negotiations over Chinese Eastern Railway 29

Soviet Russia Insists on Original Position Ineffective Direct Negotiations by Puppet Regime Japanese Military Personnel Hinder Railway Administration (Changchun) It is currently believed here that negotiations for the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway (CER) are likely to break down. (13th Japan News Agency) (Tokyo) Regarding the negotiations for the sale of the CER, (Manchukuo) Vice Foreign Minister Ohashi met with the Soviet Union's ambassador to Japan, Yurenev, and discussed the matter for two and a half hours from 4:00 PM to 6:25 PM today, without achieving any results. Vice Foreign Minister Ohashi is scheduled to depart from Tokyo for Manchukuo on the 14th. Judging from this situation, the CER negotiations are completely stalled and can be said to be on the verge of collapse. Soviet newspapers are competing to publish anti-Japanese remarks, exposing the current state of the CER, such as banditry, and claiming that these disturbances are all instigated by Japan, considering it a form of blackmail by Japan. It is divided into two special zones. The first zone strictly prohibits foreigners from entering, so the area will be excluded from the scope of activity, and there will be no railway employees or management. The second zone (including the town of Suifenhe) is allowed to enter, but it is forbidden to construct any buildings, defenses, afforestation, or other surveying projects in the area, and violators will be subject to heavy penalties. Rutai also reported to the Ministry of Railways that the various regulations set by the Japanese military are used to prohibit the CER authorities from managing the railway affairs in the area and from making necessary repairs to the railway property. At the same time, there are also reports that the Japanese-Manchukuo police have begun a movement against the clubs of the CER employees and workers. These clubs were only restored a few days ago after repeated requests from the Soviet Union's consul. A certain police station has strictly sealed off the club at the Handaohezi (translated) station, and there is no reason for the closure. (12th TASS Telegram) (Harbin) Today, official sources released the details of the Soviet plot to assassinate a large number of Japanese and (Manchukuo) officials, causing a great shock. It is said that this case was discovered when a Russian watchman hired by the Japanese military committee in Suifenhe was killed. The list of people targeted for assassination included the director of the Japanese military committee, the commander of the Japanese military police, important (Manchukuo) government officials, and the patrol chief of the CER Suifenhe police station. More than 30 Soviet Russians related to the case have been arrested. The Japanese military authorities also claim that there are documents proving that the Soviet military command in Khabarovsk ordered (Chinese bandits to destroy the CER train in the area near Yimianpo). Trend of the Eastern European Pact 34

Opposition from Germany and Poland (London) If the hopes of the major politicians can be realized, a system of peace pacts and defense alliances will soon be established to ensure peace in Europe. The Eastern European Pact, which France recently conformed to the Soviet Union's intention and obtained the support of Britain and Italy, is one end. The pact covers seven countries: Germany, Czechoslovakia, Poland, Latvia, Lithuania, Estonia, and Soviet Russia. Each signatory country should not only respect other signatory countries but also assist them in resisting aggression from another signatory country or a country outside the pact. Although France is not a signatory country, it is the guarantor of the pact. The main point is that France guarantees the western border of the Soviet Union, the Soviet Union guarantees the eastern border of France, and Germany and the Soviet Union guarantee the Polish border. Except for Germany and Poland, all related countries and some countries without direct relations have approved the pact. Germany's attitude is very indifferent, believing that the net cast by the pact is nothing more than to make Germany recognize the borders delineated by the Treaty of Versailles. Unless France recognizes Germany's military equality, it is impossible to make Germany comply. There is also a price to pay for Poland to accept the pact. Poland claims that its ally Romania should participate in the pact and requires that each signatory country guarantee the current Polish-Lithuanian border in order to have all countries recognize the legality of its annexation of the Vilnius region. If the seven-power pact fails, we can believe that France, Soviet Russia, and Czechoslovakia will sign a three-power defense alliance and put Germany in a great encirclement. The so-called Eastern European Locarno Pact will be related to other important treaties. First, the pact will be combined with the Western European Locarno Pact signed by Germany, France, Britain, Italy, and Belgium in 1925 to guarantee the borders of Germany and France and Belgium. Second, the pact will also be related to the Little Entente, with Czechoslovakia as the key role in the Eastern European Locarno system. (13th National Telegram)

US Increases Gold Price Rumor 40

Senator Thomas of Chicago advocates immediately raising the price of gold to $41.34 per ounce, in accordance with the maximum price stipulated in the 1933 Gold Act. Speaking at the Century of Progress Exhibition, Thomas insisted that inflating the currency is the only way to offset the current excessive purchasing power of gold and restore the gold standard value of 1926 under Coolidge. Thomas urged the government to take drastic steps to relieve debt and save the majority of the nation trapped in debt. Thomas stated that this relief can only be achieved through currency inflation. A gold price of $41.34 is double the previous statutory value and equal to that of a silver half-dollar, enabling debtors to repay their debts with dollars of the same value as when they borrowed. Currently, debtors must pay between $1.35 and $1.50 for every dollar of debt borrowed during commercial prosperity and boom times, and immediately raising the current gold price (currently $35 per ounce) is the most reasonable and effective method of his proposed inflation policy. Thomas continued, broadly using silver will also help the country's economic recovery. Preparing silver as part of the national currency is the second practical way to reduce the purchasing power of gold. It is generally believed that Mr. Thomas' speech today is a harbinger of future inflationary movements. (National Telegram, 13th)

American Antarctic Exploration 41

(Washington) Rear Admiral Byrd, a famous American explorer, set out with his team from the Bay of Little America in Virginia on October 22 last year for his second Antarctic expedition. Before departing, Byrd firmly stated that this expedition was not aimed at flying over the South Pole, but rather at continuing to collect materials about an unexplored land area almost the size of South America. His main base was set up in the Bay of Wales, and Byrd inspected from a camp 123 miles away, where he spent the winter. Byrd subsequently fell into a dangerous situation due to the melting ice. Today, the National Geographic Society received news that Byrd had been rescued. Although physically weak, his spirit was still good. The rescue team, led by Dr. Poulter, set off from Little America on August 8. After two failures, they finally reached Byrd's observation post. The first two attempts were driven back by strong winds. On Wednesday of last week, they made a third attempt, and with the help of specially made snowmobiles, they succeeded. (Reuters, 12th)

French and German Train Accidents 42

A fast train between Avignon, Geneva, and Ventimiglia, France, derailed at this station at 4:00 this morning. All eight passenger cars derailed, and the locomotive and postal car collided with a freight train parked on a parallel line, causing the freight train to also derail. After the accident, all the lights in the station went out. Rescue workers rushed to the scene, but due to the darkness, rescue was difficult. The locomotive of the fast train caught fire, threatening to spread to the passenger cars, so the rescue workers first focused on this. The injured moaned and cried out in pain, a tragic scene to behold. The number of dead and injured is not yet known, but it is known that there were no British or American passengers on the train. Rescue workers carried the injured out of the train and into the station for first aid, and also summoned nearby doctors to come and provide assistance. All four main lines at Avignon station were blocked and are currently being cleared. The cause of the accident is unknown, but many believe it was caused by the fast train traveling at excessive speed. Many police officers have also been dispatched to the accident site to assist in the rescue work, and officials are currently conducting an investigation. (Reuters, 12th) (Berlin) Two trains collided in Herne, Westphalia, today, resulting in the deaths of two passengers, serious injuries to seventeen, and minor injuries to one hundred and forty-three. All were German nationals; no foreign passengers were involved. (Reuters, 12th)

Disputes in German Churches 43

(Berlin) Several members of the Emergency League of Pastors in Berlin and various provinces were arrested today for reading a document from the pulpit that severely criticized Archbishop Müller and the National Conference of the German Evangelical Church. The document quoted scripture to denounce the various unjust laws passed by the so-called National Conference, stating that anyone who obeys these laws violates the church constitution and that they therefore refuse to comply and urge all church members not to commit the crime of violating the church constitution. The National Conference of Churches recently passed a law recognizing all actions taken by church administrators since Müller assumed the office of Archbishop, including the suspension of clergy. (Reuters, 12th)

General Strike in Havana 44

Bombings Occur Everywhere Havana today marks the first anniversary of the overthrow of former President Machado's government. A general strike has broken out throughout the city's transportation system, along with riots and multiple bombings. A bomb exploded at a Nationalist political club, seriously injuring two women. This is indeed a prelude to demonstrations in the Cuban capital. After the bombings, the police immediately took action, and vehicles and pedestrians near the political club were inspected, but the authorities did not capture any trace of the bomber. The general strike by transportation workers has obvious political undertones. National telephone, telegraph, and wireless communications have all been suspended. Although the strikers demanded the immediate release of reinstatement money, it is heard that the real reason for the strike is that the workers insist on dismissing all officials who had previously participated in the Machado government. President Madieta convened a cabinet meeting and immediately ordered transportation workers to resume work first, while the government would consider the workers' demands within forty-eight hours, but the government's proposal has been rejected by labor leaders. Workers at the power plant then held a meeting to decide to strike in support of transportation workers. Madieta immediately mobilized troops, and armed patrols were densely deployed near all main roads, power plants, and public utilities. The government's drastic steps have made the demonstrators lose courage. The whole city is relatively quiet tonight, but there are still bombings in the suburbs, but they have not caused major disasters. (National Telegram, 12th) Havana The strike situation here has not changed. Telegraphic communication remains blocked. Fifty-two strikers from various agencies under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation have been arrested and detained in the fortress overnight without release. (Havas, 12th)

Spanish Ex-Prince

Dies in Car Accident in Vienna 46

Vienna Prince Gonzalo, the fourth son of the Spanish ex-King Alfonso, died in a car accident in Vienna today. The car was being driven by Princess Beatriz, the ex-King's daughter, who swerved to avoid an oncoming motorcycle, causing the car to crash into a stone wall. The accident occurred at about 7:30 PM on Sunday. At the time, both siblings were injured, but the injuries were considered minor, so they returned to the villa. The prince then felt unwell and urgently summoned a doctor, but before the doctor arrived, the prince had already died of a ruptured stomach blood vessel. His father, ex-King Alfonso, was by his side when he died, and his sister suffered minor injuries and is unharmed. The motorcyclist was subsequently arrested by the police for drunk driving and causing the accident. (National Telegram, 13th) Vienna Prince Gonzalo, the fourth son of the Spanish ex-King Alfonso, went out for a drive with his sister yesterday. While traveling near Klagenfurt, they suddenly collided with a bicycle and then crashed into a wall on the side of the road, causing Gonzalo to suffer abdominal injuries. He was rushed to the hospital and famous doctors were called in for treatment, but his injuries were too severe, and he died here today at the age of only twenty. (Reuters, 13th)

Soviet Russia's Heavy Industry 47

Situation in the First Half of 1934 (TASS Moscow Correspondence, July 10) According to the basic figures of the People's Commissariat of Heavy Industry, the Soviet Union's annual plan for heavy industry in 1934 was 47% or 48% complete in the first half of the year. In the first half of the year, the percentage of completion of the annual plan in heavy industry was the highest on record. In June, the total output of heavy industry was worth 9.4 billion rubles, an increase of 28% over the same period last year, and more than 3.1 billion rubles more than the total output for the entire year of 1930. Production increased by 28%, while the labor force only increased by 10.2%, indicating a significant increase in labor productivity. The average output per worker can be increased by 16.5%. Compared with 1933, the cost of production in the first quarter of 1934 decreased by 5%, and in April it decreased by 7.1%. The following are the results of various important sectors of heavy industry in the first half of the year: The total coal production was 44 million tons, compared to 34.6 million tons in the same period last year, an increase of 26.9%. The total pig iron production was 4,910,000 tons, exceeding the same period last year by 54.7%, completing 49.1% of the annual plan. In the same period of 1933, only 35.4% was completed, and in the same period of 1932, only 32.5% was completed. The pig iron production in the first half of this year exceeded the total production for the entire year of 1929. The total steel production was 4,491,000 tons, exceeding the same period last year by 48.4%. The total rolled steel production was 3,090,000 tons, an increase of 36.1% over the same period last year. Labor productivity in the first five months of this year increased by 29.7%, so production costs decreased by 7.2%. This is in comparison to 1933. In terms of oil production, the total amount of mixed oil was 11,845,000 tons, and the total amount of refined oil was 645,000 tons, an increase of 18.7% and 75%, respectively, over the same period last year in various regions. Compared with the same period last year, the increase in other heavy industry sectors is as follows: aluminum by three times, locomotives by 33%, freight trains by 50.7%, freight cars by 34.2%, automobiles by 239%, tractors (from the Stalingrad and Kharkov plants) by 275.79%, copper sulfide by 67.4%, sulfuric acid by 35.8%, acid phosphate by 36.1%, and ammonium sulfate by 30.440%.

Submarine Adventure Story 48

Bermuda Dr. Beebe, a famous American marine biologist, stated here today the circumstances of his exploration in a steel ball 2,500 feet deep into the sea, the purpose of which was to collect important scientific data and investigate five or six kinds of strange fish never heard of before, so he landed on the seabed two days ago, breaking the world record. He found giant phosphorescent strange fish half a mile underwater, glowing all over their bodies, shimmering like the stars in the sky. This fish pounced on the ball he was riding in, and the light burst forth like fireworks, but after an hour and twenty-five minutes underwater, because the supply of oxygen was gradually exhausted, he could not continue to descend, and so the ball was dragged up by a tugboat. Dr. Beebe is 57 years old and has been an honorary curator of birds at the New York Zoological Park since 1899, and the director of the institute's scientific research division, and a member of the Zoological Society of London. He has won many awards and has written many papers on birds and their evolution. His most recent work is "Tropical Seashore I," etc. (Reuters, 13th)

Public Telegram 92

A telegram from the Drought Relief Committee of Guichi County, Anhui, to the Shanghai Shen Bao office to be forwarded to various newspaper offices, charitable organizations, and disaster relief agencies: The drought in Guichi is severe, food is scarce, and the people are on the verge of death, with no guarantee for the next day. Regarding the actual situation of the disaster in the county this year, apart from the newly reclaimed polder land along the river where beans and miscellaneous grains can only yield 20% of the harvest, the majority of the farmland, totaling over 30,000 mu, which is subject to regular taxation, is all located in depressions and relies on rainwater for irrigation. During the early spring rice transplanting season, prolonged cold weather delayed the growth of seedlings. By early summer, temperatures gradually rose, and because the reservoirs dried up, irrigation was untimely, causing the rice plants to wither. In addition, continuous drought and scorching heat turned the lush greenery into scorched stubble. According to statistics, the loss of rice this time is estimated to be over 1.2 million shi, which is ten times worse than previous years of flooding. It is a rare catastrophe in centuries. Currently, the situation in the rural areas is precarious. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and the people are already panicking about food. They are unable to save themselves and can only look to the heavens for sustenance. Feeling the pain deeply, we send this telegram to call for help. We implore your newspaper to embrace the spirit of universal aid, with sympathy in your hearts. You have always valued humanity and served as the voice of the people. Therefore, we earnestly request that you publish the tragic situation of our county's disaster in your newspaper. If you could show compassion and grant us relief, the virtue of rebirth would be bestowed upon us by your esteemed newspaper. Sincerely, Drought Relief Committee of Guichi County, Anhui. Survey by the Sichuan Pacification Committee.

Detailed Information on the Bandit Area of Wanyuan 93

Rural Areas Bankrupt, People Sit and Wait to Die.

People's Militia Resist Communists, Killing Thousands of Bandits.

Epidemics Spread, Coffins Become Empty. Chengdu Air Mail Report: The Sichuan bandits have been holding out in Wanyuan for almost two years. The people have resisted the Communists barehanded, one after another, seizing thousands of bandits' weapons and killing thousands of bandits. Although Wanyuan City has been gained and lost three times, the bandits have not been driven out of the territory. However, their brave, resolute, and indomitable spirit is truly commendable. Therefore, we record the recent survey report by Zhou Bao Han and other members of the Sichuan Pacification Committee on the recovered area of Wanyuan on the left:

Page 10

Rural Bankruptcy 94

During this inspection, we traveled more than 300 li within Wanyuan. We saw very few farmers in the fields, and less than half of the rice paddies had been planted. It is said that farmers avoid conscription during the day and quietly plant at night. The anti-bandit army (such as the units of Liu Guangyu and Yang Guozhen) also helped with planting. The land is completely barren. After the wheat harvest, farmers mostly rely on potatoes, wheat, and barley for food, but the harvest is meager and quickly exhausted. In the sixth and seventh lunar months (the autumn harvest in Wanyuan is usually around mid-August), farmers are left with empty pots. Before Chengkou fell, the corn imported from there was still sufficient to provide relief. Now, although Chengkou has been recovered, the source of food is still difficult to secure for the time being. This requires finding a way to provide relief. In past years, Wanyuan produced about 3,000 jin of white fungus and about 200,000 jin of tea in the spring, worth about 300,000 yuan. This was enough to boost the city's economy, and farmers used it to exchange for rice, food, and utensils. Now, both tea and fungus are gone, and they are sitting and waiting to die. Able-bodied men and women are rarely seen in farmhouses. Either they have been forcibly conscripted by the Communists, died of disease at home, or are lying sick in bed. Those who have not experienced it firsthand may not believe this phenomenon.

Epidemics 95

Another terrible phenomenon in the recovered area is the prevalence of epidemics, with a large number of deaths. The people in the county, having been under the bandits for a long time, those who fled and those who remained, all feel that their lives are out of order. In addition, the Communists killed too many people, all buried shallowly. The Communists killed by the Sacred Mother Corps were left unburied in the fields. After a long time, the stench of corpses spread everywhere. Since the beginning of spring, a major epidemic has broken out. Medicine is in short supply, and once infected, people can only sit and wait to die. As a result, deaths are rampant and difficult to stop. The average number of deaths per household is two or more, and there are also reports of entire families of more than ten people dying. Coffins everywhere have long been used up. It is common to see wealthy families unable to find a wooden coffin for their parents after they die, and they cannot keep the bodies at home for long, so they are mostly buried simply (wrapped in mats). The deaths of soldiers and laborers are also everywhere, especially among the laborers. The symptoms of the epidemic are initially dizziness and pain, followed by fever all over the body, thirst, panic, chest tightness, and loss of appetite. If the medicine is administered properly (usually Chonghe Tang), a large amount of sweat will be expelled from the body, which is called "turning sweat." After turning sweat, further relief can be given with a soothing agent (roughly Minor Bupleurum Decoction plus White Tiger Decoction), and gradual recovery will be achieved. If there is no major sweat within one, three, or five days after taking the medicine, it is very dangerous. If there is no sweat for seven days, death is certain. During the turning of sweat, some may also experience nosebleeds, which is called "turning red sweat." This is a sign that danger can be avoided.

Militia Resistance 96

In mid-October of last year, the Communists came to attack. The stationed troops were ordered to abandon Wanyuan. The Wanyuan regular militia, unable to retreat in time, the entire Second Platoon was surrounded by the Communists. The regular militia and civilians then gradually gathered in Qishugou, Guankouping, Kuchouping, and other places on the border of Xuanhan and Kaixian counties, totaling about 1,000 men and guns. Because the head of the militia bureau, Zhu, had fled to Wanxian early, Zhang Ziyi, the head of the public security bureau, was publicly elected to lead the resistance against the Communists. At that time, supplies were difficult, and the enemy was pursuing closely. The hardship and suffering were self-evident. Later, contact was made with Chen Guoshu, the commander of the Chengwan guerrilla forces, and they were placed under his command and organized into two detachments, totaling about ten companies. Supplies were also provided by him gradually, but cotton clothing and bedding were lacking. They have suffered greatly in the snowy and icy weather. Starting on January 3rd of this year, the militia counterattacked and recovered the entire territory of the second and third districts with the support of the villagers, only 60 li from Wanyuan City. On February 4th, the Communists launched a counterattack with the main force of three or four regiments and a special task battalion. The militia was unable to resist, and they were reinforced by the Jinxiong and Yu detachments, but they were still unable to resist. They then retreated to the Hongmiaozi and Fanhuai stores area on the Xuanwan border. On March 20th, when they attacked the Gujunba of Wanyuan again, the Sacred Mother Corps had already defeated the bandits. The county seat was recovered, and the militia entered the city to help defend it. Xun's and Du's detachments from Wang Sanchun's unit also entered the city one after another, for about a week. The bandits increased their main force to counterattack, and the militia was caught off guard and unprepared, so they abandoned it again and retreated to Baisha River and Qinghua Creek, 60 li from the city. On April 17th, the militia, in conjunction with Chen Guoshu's entire force, Jin Zhitang's unit of Wanyuan civilians, and Yang Shiyuan's unit of the Sacred Mother Corps, recaptured the county seat. On May 2nd, the bandits counterattacked again, and it fell again on the 4th. The various units still retreated to their original lines. Currently, due to deaths in battle, deaths from epidemics, and returns home due to illness, only about half of the militia is defending the front line against the bandits.

People's Anti-Communism 97

When the Communists occupied Wanyuan, most of the people who fled were former and current government employees, accounting for no more than one-tenth. A large number of people stayed at home. After the Communists came, they reversed the traditional customs of the people and brutally murdered them. As a result, the people of the second, third, eighth, ninth, and tenth districts of Wanyuan resisted the Communists four times in November and December of last year and January and February of this year, remotely echoing the militia. They slaughtered many Communists and killed quite a few Communist political personnel. Quan Zhitang's unit in the second district was able to resist the bandits from beginning to end and attacked very vigorously. Quan is a man from Caojiagou, about 60 years old, who once served as a regimental leader. He has several sons, all of whom are farmers, strong and able, who assist their father in mobilizing the people of Caojiagou to firmly defend and not flee. They occasionally led the villagers to attack the bandits' Soviet, but when they lacked food and utensils, they would confiscate the villages where the bandits concentrated food and utensils to replenish their supplies. During the months when Wanyuan was in the bandit area, Caojiagou alone was able to preserve itself. Sometimes they even lured the bandits deep into an ambush, and none of the bandits escaped.

The Sacred Mother Corps' Military Achievements 98

At first, the people thought that even if the Communists came, they would not cut off their lifeline. When they saw the increasing harm caused by the Communists, the people became determined to resist the Communists, and guerrilla units defected one after another. The bandits believed that the people of Wanyuan could not be utilized, so they carried out large-scale massacres and set fires everywhere. At this time, the people were desperate and prayed day and night to the gods they believed in to save them. This is how the Sacred Mother Corps was born, or perhaps it was a type of hypnosis. According to the Corps' proclamation, "The Red Bandits have plagued Sichuan for years, and the people have been displaced and died in droves. Among them, brave people have resisted the Communists many times, but they have not achieved complete victory. Fortunately, Wu Xiling, who has been farming for generations and enjoys doing good deeds, witnessed the rampant behavior of the Red Bandits and appealed to the Sacred Mother to save the people. He fasted for days, and his sincerity moved the Sacred Mother to bestow upon Xiling on the 26th day of the first month at the hour of Hai (9-11 PM), personally instructing him on the tactics of suppressing the bandits and the skills of boxing and fighting. The people were initially skeptical, but after the battle of Changba, they won three victories in three battles, and spread the word to various churches to establish the Sacred Mother Corps for suppressing bandits and saving the people. As a result, they captured more than a dozen market towns, recovered Wanyuan City, and obtained a machine gun and countless bullets. They also strictly ordered that they not take anything from the people." Before the third month of the lunar calendar, the Corps fought dozens of battles, large and small, with the bandits, and always won with fewer against more. According to reliable investigations, at least a thousand real Red Bandits were killed. At that time, the Communists were terrified at the mere mention of their name and seemed ready to flee at the sight of them. They called them the "Bladder Soldiers" and paid close attention to preventing them. After the bandits understood the situation of the Corps, they avoided them in fortifications to deal with them, and sometimes took advantage of the night to surround and burn the crowds inside the Sacred Mother Corps' churches, resulting in mutual casualties. Moreover, the Corps lacked supplies, organization, and training, relying solely on wooden knives and other weapons to resist the bandits, who were capable of raging frenzy. It is only right that they could only sustain a single burst of energy. However, at present, in the second, third, and eighth districts, there are still many of its members, who often coordinate with the anti-bandit army in combat and serve as vanguards. An investigation revealed that the members of the Corps are all rural farmers with dark faces. The weapons they use are wooden knives and wooden sticks, with knife and axe teams following behind. The leader is a general or child in red clothing, leading the way with a duster in hand. In times of emergency, with a single call along the way, women and children would follow, and farm tools and wooden sticks would all become weapons. Their spirit of courageously advancing, pursuing and attacking bandits, fearing neither death nor surrender, has caused the Communists to retreat three times in awe. (Omitted below)

Severe Flooding in Henan Province 99

＝Rivers Rise Due to Continuous Torrential Rains＝

＝Dozens of Counties Suffer Major Disasters＝ Kaifeng Correspondence: Due to continuous torrential rains in Henan Province, rivers have risen sharply. Dozens of counties, including Shangcai, Shangshui, Linying, Fengqiu, Suiping, Runan, Yancheng, Xiping, Wuyang, Tanghe, Yexian, Xihua, Fangcheng, Xiangcheng, Fugou, Taikang, Yanling, Weishi, Biyang, Qinyang, and Xin'an, have suffered disasters. Recently, many counties have reported flooding to the Provincial Relief Association. According to Changge County, heavy rains fell for three days, the 24th, 25th, and 26th of last month, and the Bo River overflowed, destroying more than 2,900 houses and inundating more than 24,000 mu of farmland in 19 villages including Dongfuzhuang. More than 1,000 houses were destroyed and more than 30,000 mu of farmland were inundated in 17 villages including Tianwucun. The Linying River also breached its banks, and the water depth from Shangzhuang in the Second District to Pingning City and other places was more than ten feet, navigable by boat, destroying more than 1,700 qing of land. Heavy rains fell again on the 5th of this month, and more than five zhang of the county city wall collapsed. The first, third, and fourth districts suffered severe damage again. After the rain in Tongxu, boats could sail on land and reach Fugou. Fifty li from Nandaizhuang to Xiaoqinggang and other villages in Taikang became a vast swamp. In Baofeng, the water depth was several feet, and the disaster was particularly severe in the third and fourth districts due to the overflowing of the Sha River. Yancheng suffered two floods, and all 7,000 qing of autumn crops were submerged, with less than 20% remaining. The Sha River breached its banks in five places, the Li River and the Gan River each breached their banks in four places, and the Ying River breached its banks in twenty places. The most tragic was Heya Li Village on the banks of the Sha River, where the houses, food, livestock of more than 200 households were completely washed away. More than 50 other villages were also affected, and more than 100,000 victims were all living outdoors and exposed to the elements. (August 11) Shaanxi Province

Overview of Population Distribution 100

Continuous Years of Famine Lead to Extremely Low Population Density

Shanxi Residents Dominate Shaanxi's Commerce. Xi'an Correspondence: The ethnic issues in the Northwest have become extremely serious, but the migration of people to the Northwest is still not being paid attention to. Here is a brief description of the investigation in Shaanxi:

Population Density 101

According to a survey by the Shaanxi Autonomous Region Preparatory Office in 1924, the population of Shaanxi was 21,193,351. In September 1933, the Ministry of Interior, based on the statistical report of 1930, the population of Shaanxi was 10,296,531. In 1932, a survey by the Shaanxi Civil Affairs Department showed that the population of Shaanxi was 9,752,015. The first two surveys were too long ago and may not be accurate. Although the third survey was only two years ago, in the past year (1933), the counties in Shaanxi that suffered from water, drought, wind, hail, black frost, bandits, epidemics, and plague accounted for two-thirds and a half of all counties in the province, so it seems unreliable. According to a survey by the Party Headquarters, the population of Wugong County has decreased by more than two-thirds since the famine. By analogy, the number of people reduced in Shaanxi over the years will definitely not be less than 500,000. According to the investigations of recent academic groups and various surveyors and highway surveyors, all say that there is too much wasteland in the counties of Shaanxi. This can also indirectly prove that the population of Shaanxi is not large. In short, the current population of Shaanxi cannot exceed 9 million. If this population is compared with the area of Shaanxi, which is 195,067 square kilometers, the average number of people per square kilometer is less than five (based on Zeng Shiying's estimate of the area of Shaanxi). The scarcity of population density can be seen here. At the same time, the reason why residents of neighboring provinces with higher population densities migrate westward is not difficult to understand. Among the residents who have migrated to Shaanxi from neighboring provinces, Shanxi, Henan, and Shandong provinces account for the most. The number of residents who have migrated to Shaanxi from other provinces is relatively small.

Shanxi Residents 102

The people who have migrated to Shaanxi from Shanxi are distributed in the widest area, but most are in northern Shaanxi and Guanzhong. There are many Shanxi people in Yulin and Fuguo in northern Shaanxi, and Tongguan, Chaoyi, Dali, Chang'an, Xianyang, Sanyuan in Guanzhong. Almost all of them are engaged in business. Eight out of ten of the larger businesses in Shaanxi are run by Shanxi people. Among them, the salt industry, sauce gardens, groceries, and silver firms are almost monopolized by Shanxi people. The saying that Shanxi people are good at business is by no means an exaggeration. I once saw a couplet on the door of a salt store in Xi'an that said, "Transporting a piece of jade from eastern Jin, exchanging it for ten thousand taels of gold from western Qin." It is indeed a true portrayal of the people of Shanxi. The ways that Shanxi people enter Shaanxi are: (1) Crossing the Yellow River from Fenglingdu, taking the road to Tongguan and westward; (2) Crossing the Yellow River near Qikou in Shanxi, passing through Wubao and Suide, southward, or northward through Mizhi to Yulin; (3) Crossing the Yellow River near Baode in Shanxi to Fuguo, passing through Shenmu to Yulin; (4) Crossing the Yellow River from Puzhou (Yongji) in Shanxi through Daqing Pass (Pujin Pass), passing through Chaoyi and Dali, to Weinan County; (5) Crossing the Yellow River from Yongheguan in Yonghe County, Shanxi, to Yanchuan County; (6) Crossing the Yellow River from Liulin Ferry in Yongning County, Shanxi, to Wubao County. Among them, Tongguan is the main road, and there is the most traffic.

Henan Residents 103

Residents who moved from Henan to Shaanxi mostly live scattered in areas south of the Han River, north of Shaanxi, and in counties stretching westward from Tongguan to Changwu. Their concentration points are in places like Chang'an, Nanzheng (i.e., Hanzhong), and Longju Village. They are mostly employed in handicrafts (coppersmiths, blacksmiths, barrel makers, cooks, carpenters) and manual labor (rickshaw pullers, boat pushers). The Henan residents in the Guanzhong area are mostly from Luoyang, Gongxian, Sishui, Wuzhi, Qinyang, Wenxian, and the Heishiguan area. The Henan residents in southern Shaanxi are mostly from Xichuan, Nanyang, and Lushi. Henan residents have the highest mobility. Every year after the old lunar year, people coming from west of Luoyang arrive in groups, each carrying a shoulder pole of goods, one after another, heading towards Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, and other areas. They sell their goods as they go, and once sold, they return to places like Chang'an to wholesale more goods and head west again. Sometimes they make several such trips, eventually stopping in Gansu or Ningxia. Once they arrive, they buy local medicinal materials (such as licorice, goji berries, rhubarb, safflower, Tibetan green fruit) and carry them back to Henan for sale, or they buy ponies and drive them to the vicinity of Chang'an for sale. Quite a few people have become wealthy using this method. These people are extremely familiar with the conditions along the way, and there are many fellow villagers in major county towns (mostly engaged in photography and groceries), so the journey is peaceful and without unexpected dangers. There are four routes that Henan people take to enter Shaanxi: (1) from Tongguan through Huayin, Huaxian, Weinan, and Lintong westward; (2) from Shanzhou by Yellow River boat westward; (3) from Jingziguan, B亭, and Xichuan County, going upstream on the Dan River westward; (4) from Lushi County in Henan, through Muxianggou and Suxia, to Luonan in Shaanxi. The first two routes are the main routes for Henan to enter Shaanxi.

Shandong Residents 104

People who moved from Shandong to Shaanxi mostly live along the Wei River area, such as in Lintong, Sanyuan, and other places, where their footprints are abundant. Most of them are engaged in agriculture, and they like to live in groups to help and protect each other. The Shandong residents in the cities mostly engage in cloth and silk trade or drive large carts, going west to Gansu and Ningxia (there are many Shandong people in Ningxia). Shandong people entering Shaanxi mostly take the Tongguan route.

Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hebei Residents 105

Since the Longhai Railway was extended to Tongguan, merchants from Tianjin and Hebei have set up branches in places like Xi'an in order to expand their businesses. Therefore, most of the Hebei residents currently in Shaanxi are engaged in hardware, foreign goods, military clothing, leather, cloth, sundries, photography, and medicinal materials. Those engaged in labor are mostly involved in driving cars and repairing cars. There are also many Hebei natives in the administrative circles. Since the government has focused on the actual development of the Northwest, more and more people from Jiangsu and Zhejiang have come to Shaanxi, but most of them live in Chang'an and hold positions in the political circles. After the September 18th Incident, the commerce of the Southeast was affected by the decline, and it was necessary to find other ways to develop. Therefore, there are many shops in Chang'an operated by people from Jiangsu and Zhejiang, such as cigarette, silk, foreign goods, bookstore, and bank shops. There are not many Guangdong natives in Shaanxi, and most of them are engaged in photography. There are also one or two in the administrative circles. There is currently no accurate survey of how many people from other provinces are in Shaanxi. In short, Shaanxi's population density is very low. For the sake of the country's future and the survival of the nation, it is necessary to increase Shaanxi's population as soon as possible.

Opium Poison 106

The reasons for the decline in Shaanxi's population are: (1) natural disasters, (2) man-made disasters, (3) opium, (4) diseases, such as trachoma, scabies, and goiter, which have become the most common diseases among Shaanxi people, (5) infanticide. It is said that in Yongshou and other areas in western Shaanxi, families often kill any children born after raising three children in order to reduce the burden. This kind of tragedy may also be caused by difficult living conditions. The healthiest ethnic group in the Northwest is the Hui people. They neither smoke opium nor have other bad habits, and their solidarity is particularly strong. This is truly the most promising ethnic group in our nation. Song Education Institution Presents to Chairman Chen.

Please Thoroughly Investigate the Grain Tax Corruption Case 107

Song report: Wu Baohuang, member of the Jiangsu Education Funds Management Office, Zhu Zhaosheng, director of the Songjiang Education Bureau, and others, petitioned Chairman Chen to thoroughly investigate the oppression and corruption case. The original petition stated that the Songjiang County government colluded to use the opportunity of converting land into grain transport and reducing the rent to jointly embezzle tens of thousands of yuan in tax money, damaging education funds. The case investigation found that the old Huating jurisdiction of this county included 34,639 mu, 1 li, and 6 si of converted land in the north of the Pu River, and 84,960 mu, 3 fen, 5 li, and 1 hao, 2 si in the south of the Pu River. In the 18th year of the Republic of China, when She Yingduo was the director of the Finance Bureau, he was ordered to convert it to grain transport and create a register for it, which was handled by the head of the Jingzheng Section, Che Zhao (a native of Songjiang), who is now the head of the Finance Section. The converted grain transport in the north of the Pu River was 3,260 shi, 6 dou, 4 sheng, and 9 ge, and each business household has cleared it annually. The converted grain transport in the south of the Pu River was 7,039 shi, 8 dou, 6 sheng, and 3 ge, and not all of the business households have fully paid. In summary, the annual levy of converted grain transport is about 5,000 shi or more. The price of each shi of grain transport was 5 yuan and 7 jiao in the 18th year, 7 yuan and 9 jiao in the 19th and 20th years, and 7 yuan and 7 jiao in the 21st year, averaging 7 yuan and 3 jiao. Ye Zongcheng, the director of the First Land Tax Collection Office, had a history of arrears and misappropriation. However, this item of approximately 10,300 shi of converted grain transport was included in the amount of actual levies and uncollected amounts in the autumn surveys over the years, and the Finance Bureau and the County Government filled in the forms and reported them, which can be verified. Che Zhao was the section chief during the tenure of former directors Shen Bingchen and Shen Binde. On May 1, last year (the 22nd year), the Finance Bureau was merged into the County Government, and County Chief Jin Tigan appointed Che Zhao as the head of the Finance Section because he was familiar with the contents of the grain counter. In September of that year, County Chief Jin, because some business households along the coast resisted completing the converted grain transport, used the method of reducing the rent to falsely claim that the coastal converted land and the converted land in the north of the Pu River were converted land in the south of the Pu River. In his reply to the Finance Department Commissioner Shen Zhengshu, he stated that more than 10,000 shi of converted grain transport in the south of the Pu River had not been received since the 18th year, and that it had to be reduced by 60% in the 22nd year and oppressively levied by 40% in the 18th year. After the Finance Department approved it, it deducted 10,299 shi, 9 dou, 5 sheng, and 2 he of converted grain transport from the amount of actual levies and uncollected amounts in the autumn surveys over the years. 10,300 shi and 6 he of converted grain transport in the 19th year, 10,300 shi, 5 dou, 1 sheng, and 2 he of converted grain transport in the 21st year, totaling 41,201 shi and 3 sheng and 8 he of converted grain transport in the north of the Pu River. However, the grain silver that the people had completed in the above four years, and the stamped coupons that had been intercepted, were not announced and returned or offset based on the coupons. (The 23rd year grain coupons notification was still created and stamped according to the unreduced amount. It is said that someone has reported it.) The amount of concealed converted grain transport that has been collected is no less than 20,000 shi, totaling about 150,000 to 160,000 yuan. About 30,000 yuan is for provincial education expenses, and about 12,000 yuan is for county education expenses. Most of the rest is for provincial funds. In June of this year, Yang Zhimin, a local, coveted the position of director of the collection office, and instigated Lu Boxin and others to file a report to the county party headquarters to expose him, first to coerce Director Ye to resign and allow Yang Zhimin's son, Yunwen, to succeed him. On July 1, County Chief Jin approved the change in order to appease the atmosphere and find a way to cover it up. But it was known to the outside world, and someone filed a complaint with the Finance Department (but the Finance Department only ordered the county to reply, which is no different from making the thief confess). The county party headquarters then decided to investigate the matters reported by Lu Boxin and sent a letter to the county to investigate thoroughly. The department committee director and bureau chief heard about it and successively reported to the county government, the education department, and the management office for instructions. County Chief Jin only sent the police to guard Director Ye on the 22nd of last month. However, County Chief Jin's instruction No. 2384 on July 18 stated that the government had heard about the alleged matters and had already ordered Ye, the former director of the First Land Tax Collection Office, to be responsible for verifying the Bao Tu, the embankment number, and the number of mu. A detailed inventory was to be prepared and sent immediately to ensure a thorough investigation. However, since this item of converted land was converted to grain transport from the 18th year, before the start of the levy in the 18th year, the grain register should have been created early, including the Bao Tu, the embankment number, the mu number, and the business household in the series of coupons. The missing coupons can be checked with the original grain register, and the collection office's general collection (etc.) ledgers and the township police's submission register can be clearly determined. Why create another inventory, causing delays and allowing those who colluded to make up for it at ease? It has been two months since this case was discovered. On what date did County Chief Jin say that the deadline was strictly limited, and until what date did it end? Why has it not been submitted or investigated? This is the first suspicious point. On August 9, County Chief Jin's Announcement No. 104 stated that in June of this year, it was discovered that the former director had collected the full amount of converted grain transport in the south of the Pu River, and that he had falsely reported the number of shi of converted grain transport in the north of the Pu River when reporting the number of shi to be reduced. However, the converted grain transport register of Dongju states that the converted grain transport in the south of the Pu River is 7,039 shi, 8 dou, 6 sheng, and 3 he, and the converted grain transport in the north of the Pu River is 3,260 shi, 6 dou, 4 sheng, and 9 he. The number of shi for converted grain transport in the north and south of the Pu River is very clear and has not been falsely reported. In September of the 22nd year, County Chief Jin and Finance Department Commissioner Shen Zhengshu jointly requested to reduce the converted grain transport by 40% in the 18th year. The original report stated that there were more than 10,000 shi of converted grain transport in the south of the Pu River, and that there had been no income since the 18th year. County Chief Jin's original report clearly does not match the grain register. Is it the confusion of County Chief Jin and the head of the responsible section, or is it the confusion of Director Ye? What kind of reasons were used for the discovery in June, and why is it still necessary to create a detailed register after two months, and to announce it on August 9? This is the second suspicious point. In short, the circumstances of this case are complex, the collusion is serious, and it involves many people. If they are not dealt with quickly and sent to the provincial law office, if it is delayed for a few weeks, they will buy back the coupons, forge ledgers, and destroy evidence, and it will be impossible to investigate. The department committee director and bureau chief have important duties and cannot remain silent. Therefore, I am responsible for reporting and have already submitted separate reports to Hall Director Zhou and Division Director Niu. I would also like to request that the head of the county government clarify the official administration and severely punish corruption, and suspend all the relevant officials of the county government and submit them to the local court in the location of the provincial government for thorough investigation and prosecution according to law. The overall situation is fortunate. Respectfully presented to Chen, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Songjiang.

Demolishing Barren Embankments 110

Causing a major disturbance. The Chenshe Town in the sixth district of the Xis district borders the Gushan Town in the fifth district of the Cheng district. At the western end of the town, there is a barren embankment that is about five zhang long and planted with trees. The project is strong. This embankment has always been a water conservancy guarantee for the surrounding farmland. This year, the weather is dry and the water is scarce. It also relies on the water from Changshu Shang Lake to flow westward. It depends on the embankment to stop the water and distribute it to the tributary rivers. The farmland is irrigated and the residents drink from the embankment. Recently, Wu Jize, the dismissed head of the Gushan Security Regiment, and Zhou Weisan, the town chief of Gushan Town, led a team of security regiment soldiers to Chenshe Town and demolished the embankment to build a wooden bridge, named Yongyu Bridge. Zhao Hongbin, the district chief of the sixth district of the Xis district, and Chen Zixiao, the town chief of Chenshe Town, learned that Wu and others should not demolish the embankment across the border, and immediately reported it to the county government and forwarded it to the Jiangyin County Government for investigation. They demolished the wooden bridge and rebuilt the embankment. Wu and others also presented separate reports to the Cheng and Xis counties, citing the convenience of transportation and irrigation of farmland, requesting that the embankment be demolished and the bridge built. The two county governments have now ordered the Construction Bureau to send personnel to conduct a joint survey with the district chiefs of the two districts to discuss a fair solution. Wu Jize and Zhou Weisan and others have led five or six hundred townspeople to prepare to demonstrate and petition during the joint survey.

Landslide and House Collapse in Xicang Town 111

Xicang Town in the Beixia Township of the Second District is a prosperous commercial market with a dense population. However, the foundation of the houses along the river on the lower bank of the town suddenly burst and sank more than four feet the night before, covering an area of more than one mu. Twenty-seven shops and houses from the Cai Family Charity Hall to the Sanji Bridge have all collapsed, with rubble all over the ground, causing considerable losses. Fortunately, the residents all fled, so there were no injuries. However, when a long bamboo pole is inserted into the holes where the soil burst, the depth cannot be measured. The danger is worrying, and there may be unexpected disasters. Business has been suspended as a result. Yesterday, Cai Hongjun and Cai Zixing, the township chiefs of the area, submitted a special report to the county government, requesting that personnel be sent to conduct an on-site survey, and forwarded to the Construction Department for review, and to provide relief and plan for the aftermath as soon as possible.

Tragic News Amidst Severe Drought 114

Since the beginning of summer, there has been no rain in this county, and traffic boats have been suspended for a month. Therefore, cases of farmers starving to death and committing suicide have been common in recent times. Some have even sold their sons and daughters to maintain their lives. Huang, a farmer in Nandu Town, used to be well-off, but his family has declined since the flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China. In addition, he has many daughters and many mouths to feed. This summer, he suddenly encountered a severe drought and was in extreme distress. At first, he pawned his household items to seek a full meal. Then, he gave up his children to maintain his remaining life. Finally, he could not find a way, and he hanged himself on the 8th. It is truly tragic. Haimen.

Traveler Commits Suicide by Taking Poison 116

The next morning, the innkeeper Gao Jingou saw that Wang's face was pale and his breathing was short. He knew something was wrong and asked him what was going on. Local News

Japanese Rice Passed off as Domestic Rice 120

Unscrupulous merchants are profit-driven. A Central News Agency report from Xiamen states that rice prices have been rising recently, and various parties have been ordering foreign rice from foreign merchants. Although the customs authorities collect foreign rice taxes, the prices are still cheaper than those on the current domestic market. It is learned that rice and grains shipped from Xiamen, although only a few hundred bags each time, have been shipped to Shanghai repeatedly, and the number is quite considerable. It is reported that the rice and grains are not produced in Fujian, but are shipped from Taiwan, which belongs to Japan, to Xiamen, and then shipped to Shanghai. The reason for this transfer is that the Fujian Customs collects only half of the foreign rice tax standard set by the Ministry of Finance, while the Shanghai Customs collects the full amount. Therefore, unscrupulous merchants ship Taiwanese rice to Shanghai via Xiamen, passing it off as domestic rice to make huge profits. Cotton Industry Control Commission.

It is reported that Hu Jingliang will study various cotton planting promotion subjects, while Chen will study various cotton planting breeding subjects. Mr. Zhang Xiaomei's Opinion 126

Seven Months of Silver Export Reaching 50 Million Yuan. According to Shen Shi News Agency, since the United States announced its silver nationalization plan, it has been making full use of silver, planning to issue silver certificates for circulation in the market. The government, in addition to taking in 200 million ounces under the nationalization order, still needs to purchase 130 million ounces of silver to meet the ratio of three-quarters gold to one-quarter silver. Since the announcement of this plan, countries using gold have felt a major threat and are devising countermeasures. Countries directly affected by the

International trade is still at a loss, not knowing what to do. The reporter of Shen Shi News Agency yesterday specially interviewed Dr. Zhang Xiaomei, director of the Economic Research Office of the Bank of China, to inquire about his views on this matter. According to Mr. Zhang's opinion, the United States' silver policy will cause China's silver reserves to decrease day by day, and it is difficult to be optimistic about the future. His remarks are recorded as follows:

Silver Export 127

According to Dr. Zhang, since the past year, the inflationary faction in the United States has been advocating for higher silver prices and a lower US dollar value, which has already made it difficult for China to export goods, while cheap goods have been imported in large quantities to stimulate consumer society, resulting in an increasingly unbalanced import and export situation and creating a huge trade deficit. More silver is flowing out. Calculated over the seven months of this year, silver flowing abroad has reached as high as 50 million yuan. It is expected that this year's silver export will reach 100 million yuan. The total amount of silver in the country is estimated to be no more than 200 million yuan, most of which is concentrated in the nine major cities of Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin. The total amount stored in rural areas is extremely limited. Since silver is concentrated in cities, it is very easy to flow out of the country. As the amount of silver in the country decreases day by day, the price of securities and banknotes will inevitably plummet, the currency will contract, and industry and commerce will stagnate, ultimately leading to extreme panic.

Relief Measures 128

Various experts have discussed many ways to deal with the US silver policy, which generally include: (A) levying export taxes, and (B) prohibiting silver exports. In China's treaty ports, most of the police power is in the hands of foreigners, and the coastline is so long that the suggestion in A is of little effect. China is originally a country with a trade deficit, and it must pay silver for purchasing foreign goods, so prohibiting silver exports is also practically impossible. According to my opinion, to deal with the US silver policy, efforts must be made in the following areas: (1) Purchase and use domestic goods. The purpose of the US silver policy is to increase prices and increase trade with China. If the Chinese people can see through their plan, they should automatically purchase and use domestic goods so that their plan cannot be realized. (2) Reduce debt. The total budget for the 23rd year of the Republic of China includes more than 25.7 million yuan in debt expenses, more than half of which is for foreign debt expenditure. This is an unavoidable fact of silver outflow and a leak in addition to the trade deficit. Even the returned portion of the Boxer Indemnity is still stipulated to be used for purchasing materials and goods from various countries, which is essentially no different from not returning it at all. Such treaties are restrictive and extremely erroneous; otherwise, a large portion of exports could also be reduced. Mr. Zhang continued, purchasing domestic goods and reducing debt are the only ways to deal with the US silver policy.

A Glimpse of Yesterday's Thunderstorm 129

Heavy Rain in Slanting Sunlight - The City Center and Hongkou Are Soaked. This summer in the city has been unusually hot and dry. Since June 25th, except for a slight drop in temperature when the hurricane struck, almost every day has been around 100 degrees Fahrenheit, with the highest reaching 104.4 degrees, breaking the new record of 63 years since the establishment of the Xujiahui Observatory. After the Beginning of Autumn, everyone said that it could be hoped for coolness, but the sultry heat remained the same, lasting for fifty-one days. Yesterday afternoon around 2 o'clock, dark clouds gathered, thunder rumbled, and lightning flashed, as if a heavy rain was about to fall. Until 3:40 or so, the city center area began to experience strong winds and showers, lasting for about twenty minutes. Around 4 o'clock, the sunlight shone obliquely, and the rain became torrential. To the west of Jiangwan, near Fudan School, there was no rain at all, and the red earth and white dust flew in the air. However, south of North Sichuan Road and Hongkou Garden, there was a heavy downpour that stopped around 5 o'clock. As the saying goes, "Summer rain is separated by the edge of the field." Even though it is now autumn, it is still like summer, and it is unknown when it will finally be cool.

Ten Thousand Spacious Houses Shelter the City's Poor 132

According to Secretary-General Yu, Mayor Wu's plan to raise one million yuan to build public housing on a large scale is now actively underway. Mayor Wu's motivation for carrying out this matter stems from the fact that there are a large number of poor people in the city. These people live a miserable life, and their residences are mostly crude and unbearable, either a thatched shed or a broken boat (i.e., a shack boat). They are not enough to withstand strong winds and heavy rains, and when a fire breaks out, it is often difficult to handle. These poor people are extremely pitiful. The municipal authorities also believe that these buildings affect the city's appearance and hinder public safety, and they have repeatedly tried to find ways to ban them. However, banning them

The Banking Association Held a Group Meeting Yesterday 133

Specifically Discussing Article 9 of the Savings Bank Law

According to Guowen News Agency, the banks in the city previously, because of Article 9 of the Savings Bank Law promulgated by the Ministry of Finance (Savings banks should deposit at least one-fourth of the total amount of savings deposits in the form of government bonds, treasury bills, and other assets with reliable guarantees in a special vault established by the Central Bank as collateral for repaying savings deposits), and the provisions stipulating that the total amount of deposits should be based on the total balance at the end of each half-year, etc., the industry expressed compliance with the principles. As for the implementation methods, further research is still needed. Therefore, the Siming, Silk Industry, Guohua, Xinhua, and Jin City banks were elected to form a group meeting to discuss the methods. At noon yesterday, representatives from the five banks, Luo Qinghua, Chen Liting, Qu Jigang, Hu Xian, and Sun Ruihuang, and Lin Kanghou, secretary-general of the Banking Association, etc., had a meal at the Banking Club on Hong Kong Road and discussed the handling of Article 9 of the Savings Bank. It was generally believed that the items to be deposited in the Central Bank's vault according to the article were government bonds, treasury bills, and other assets, but the Ministry of Finance's instructions only mentioned government bonds, treasury bills, and did not mention other assets. Moreover, if the market price of government bonds and treasury bills is calculated according to the Ministry's order, the market price fluctuates from time to time, and the amount to be deposited must also increase or decrease accordingly. All kinds of doubts should be requested from the government for explanation and revision. It was decided that (1) the industry association should submit a report to the Ministry of Finance, (2) a meeting should be convened to discuss the draft of the report, and (3) another meeting should be held on the 15th of this month (Wednesday) to continue the discussion. Later, the resettlement methods for these poor people were not taken into account at first. Mayor Wu felt compassion for this and decided to raise one million yuan to build public housing on a large scale in the city's Huxi, Pudong, Nanshi, Zhabei, and other rural areas to accommodate these poor people, so that they have a place to live. Then, the shack boats and shantytowns that hinder the city's appearance and public safety will be banned, so that it will not affect the lives of the poor, and it will be easier to achieve practical results in improving the city.

Seeking Consultation with the Banking Sector to Raise One Million Yuan 134

However, this matter is of great importance and requires at least one million yuan. Given the municipal government's recent financial situation, it is really feeling overwhelmed. However, Mayor Wu believes that this matter must be carried out no matter what, so he is now actively organizing a preparatory committee. Therefore, the realization of this matter should not be far away. Regarding the funding, there are currently several methods: either consulting with commercial firms to borrow money, or cooperating with local banks. It is currently under consideration. The construction sites of the public housing will be determined based on local conditions. However, since this project is huge and the plan for improvement cannot be accomplished in one word, Mayor Wu is still studying it in detail.
