Announcement from the Cholera Prevention Office 144

The Far Eastern Society of Tropical Medicine will hold its meeting in Beijing in early October. The Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office issued its second announcement yesterday: (1) The cholera situation in the Shanghai area, apart from the following three cases of mild symptoms, no other discoveries have been made. Therefore, the cholera in the Shanghai area can still be said to be calm. (2) The unusually hot and dry weather this summer was mentioned in the first announcement on July 13. It continued to be hot and dry until heavy rain fell between July 18 and 23. From that time until August 8, the weather was dry, and the temperature and humidity decreased slightly. On August 8, a hurricane blew in, the wind was not very strong, and at the same time, 2.36 inches of rain was obtained. (3) Among the three cases of mild cholera symptoms found, the first case was a servant woman, 36 years old, who lived in Nanshi. She fell ill on July 16 and was admitted to the Public Concession Industrial Bureau Isolation Hospital on the 19th. She was hospitalized for ten days. The disease was very mild and she recovered after saline injection. Her feces were tested twice and cholera vibrio was found. The second case was a male factory worker, 25 years old, who lived in the Public Concession. He fell ill on July 17 and was sent to the Shihhsiao Hospital the next day. His symptoms were also very mild and he recovered after treatment. The third case was a 24-year-old woman, unemployed, who lived in the French Concession. She went to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital for treatment on July 28. She did not stay in the hospital for long and left after being treated, and also recovered without saline injection. Cholera bacteria were found in the feces of all three patients. However, the diseases they contracted were not very serious. It is worth noting that none of the three people had been vaccinated against cholera. The origin of the infection is unknown. All three people drank tap water, not well water or river water. They had also not visited patients with the disease. Since July 28, there have been no further discoveries of cholera. (4) The epidemic hospitals established by the Industrial Bureau and philanthropists mentioned in the first announcement are all prepared to accommodate patients. However, although the weather this year has been very hot, it can still be called an extremely calm year. The number of inpatients and outpatients this year has decreased compared with previous years, and not only has cholera not been prevalent, but also other summer diseases (except for heatstroke) have been less than in previous years. According to the report of the medical director of the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital, the hospital had about 400 outpatients a day last year, while this year there are only about 80 outpatients a day. (5) Public health agencies have not slackened in their epidemic prevention efforts. All tap water companies in the two concessions and the Chinese area provide free water to the poor as usual. The supply of this clean drinking water is the most important method for preventing cholera. In places where tap water plants are not convenient to set up, local authorities should dig artesian wells to protect the people. Dr. Hubble, Director of the Medical and Health Department of the Straits Settlements, said that when he was the Chief Medical Officer of Kedah Province, he discovered four major cholera epidemics between 1907 and 1914. Since the installation of tap water, this type of epidemic has not been discovered again. (6) Health propaganda is still being carried out as before. People from all walks of life should be vaccinated to protect themselves. As of the end of July, the number of people vaccinated against cholera is as follows: Shanghai City 160,000 people (approximately), Public Concession 57,165 people, French Concession 20,382 people, Railway Bureau 3,228 people, totaling 240,775 people. As of the end of June, 310,842 people. As of the end of July, 551,617 people. (7) The Epidemiology Group held its fourth meeting on August 10. In the reports received, the Shanghai Municipal Health Testing Institute tested 20 samples of suspected feces in July and 14 samples in August, all of which were negative for cholera. The Public Concession Health Department Testing Institute found cholera-like vibrio seven times, true cholera vibrio three times, and dysentery bacteria six times in 162 samples of suspected feces. (8) In order to determine the existence of true cholera vibrio or cholera-like vibrio, in addition to checking the water in rivers, wells, and ponds throughout the year, natural ice is also inspected to know if there are bacteria. However, the results obtained so far are all negative. (9) The Far Eastern Society of Tropical Medicine is scheduled to hold its ninth meeting in Nanjing from October 2 to 8. All tropical disease experts from various countries in the Far East, from India to Japan, are expected to attend the meeting. In addition to the various group meetings, a roundtable meeting will be specially opened for the cholera problem. Mr. Russell, Director of the Public Health Department of India, will be pushed as the chairman. He has rich experience in cholera during his tenure in Madras. It is hoped that in this discussion meeting, a deeper knowledge and stricter control methods can be obtained for this widespread epidemic in the East.

National Association of Accountants

Requesting the Promulgation of Bankruptcy Law 145

The National Association of Accountants submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating: "Upon investigation of the civil and commercial laws and regulations, since the establishment of our National Government, they have been promulgated successively and separately, and are generally considered complete. However, the bankruptcy law only has the draft bankruptcy law of the old Beijing government. Although it is clearly stated that it can be referred to, there is no current law that can be used as a standard. The reference and application are not binding, and it is easy to abuse by avoiding the important and taking the light. Accountants in various places are sometimes designated by the court as bankruptcy trustees, and they often suffer from the lack of a legal basis, making it difficult to handle the matter. The association is well aware of this actual situation, and hereby submits this document for review and consideration, and requests the Legislative Yuan to promulgate and implement the bankruptcy law as soon as possible so that there is a law to follow. Furthermore, Article 1 of the Accountants Regulations stipulates that accountants may act as bankruptcy trustees, because bankruptcy trusteeship involves accounting matters. It is also requested that the Ministry of Finance transfer the request to the Legislative Yuan, and that the position of bankruptcy trustee be clearly defined in the bankruptcy law as being held by accountants, so that accountants in various places can contribute to society." Anhui Province, Quanjiao Drought Relief Association Sends a Letter Seeking Relief 146

A fellow villager association was held at Guanshengyuan the day before yesterday to discuss the matter - it was decided to go to various charities today to petition for speedy relief. Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Anhui Province Quanjiao County Drought Relief Temporary Association sent personnel to Shanghai a few days ago, asking Jiang Xingsheng and other fellow villagers from the county in Shanghai to appeal to various charitable organizations for relief. According to the personnel, the county has an area of 5,500 square miles, and the disaster area has reached the entire county. The details are recorded as follows:

The Disaster Situation is Severe with Hundreds of Miles of Barren Land 147

There was no rain or snow in the county last winter, and it has suffered from severe drought again this spring. The water stored in the fields and ponds is not enough to soak the seeds. Those who tried their best to plant less than three-tenths of the land. It was hoped that rain would make up for the planting, but since the summer, the drought has become more severe, with no rain at all. Most of the planted crops have withered, and the unplanted fields are cracked. The ponds and dams are dry and the rivers have stopped flowing, forming a rare disaster that has not occurred in 60 years, with hundreds of miles of barren land.

Selling Wives and Children, Starving People Everywhere 148

The county has always been a poor area with few savings among the people. After the Xinwei flood disaster, the remaining survivors have not recovered their vitality. This spring, it has suffered from hail disasters again, and the harvest of wheat and barley has been sharply reduced. Now, it has suffered this drought disaster, and about 34,000 able-bodied men in the entire territory have been displaced. Ninety percent of the cattle have been slaughtered and eaten. The rural areas have collapsed, and ten out of ten houses are empty. Selling wives and children is often heard. Starving people are everywhere, and the tragic situation is beyond description. The residents cannot bear the remaining sufferings. Those who are pressed will risk danger and flee. Grain robbery has occurred in various villages, making it difficult to control. If relief is not sought urgently, the future of public security will be even more unbearable.

Elected Representatives to Appeal for Relief 149

Yesterday, all the fellow villagers from the county in Shanghai held a tea party at Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road to discuss the matter. In addition to the representative stating the previous situation, the climate of the county was also discussed. It was said that only buckwheat can be replanted when there is thorough rain before and after the Beginning of Autumn. Other crops are out of season. According to the investigation, disaster victims should be given relief grain and seed wheat, and large-scale emergency relief or king relief is especially needed to provide relief. Because the number of people waiting for relief is currently about 156,000, the meeting publicly elected three representatives to appeal to various charitable organizations in the port today, and plans to visit Xu Shiying, chairman of the National Government Relief Committee, to request relief. Construction of a Railway Workers' Canteen Planned 153

According to the Central News Agency, the Two-Route Transportation Department, in order to address the issue of railway workers' meals, plans to first establish a public-friendly railway workers' canteen in a suitable location at the Shanghai North Station. Clean and hygienic Chinese meals will be provided at the lowest possible prices for workers from various departments, sections, and stations along the railway line to dine. The proposed plan is as follows: (1) Meal Variety: Each person per meal will be provided with one soup, one dish (vegetables, meat, etc.), several bowls of rice or several steamed buns (supplied according to appetite), and a large teapot with free boiled water. (2) Fee Standard: The temporary fee standard is set at one dime per person per meal. If possible in the future, it will be reduced further. (3) Internal Equipment: The canteen will have separate kitchen and dining areas. The kitchen will be equipped with long tables, long benches, iron stoves, refrigerators, water buckets, etc. Other necessary auxiliary equipment will be added as needed. (The construction cost of the canteen is estimated by Engineer Feng to be approximately 500 silver dollars.) Workers dining in the canteen must first pay the meal fee and receive a meal ticket from the cashier. They will then present the ticket to the cook to receive the meal, which they will take and eat at the dining tables provided. (4) Dining Utensils: All dining utensils, such as vegetable basins and rice bowls, will be uniformly purchased in enamel to ensure durability. (5) Employment of Workers: The canteen will employ one Chinese cuisine chef to specialize in cooking meals and two kitchen workers to handle tasks such as washing ingredients, utensils, and cleaning the dining area. (6) Cleanliness Inspection: The cleanliness management officer will be responsible for providing guidance. The bureau has approved a trial implementation and instructed the department to work with the general affairs and engineering departments to survey the vacant land west of the dry bridge north of the North Station as the canteen location. Once the engineering department completes the drawings for the building and equipment, bidding for construction can begin. Tiger Brand Eng Aun Tong

Inferior Hat Blanks Replace Sample Goods

Bei Xuehai Deceives American Merchants 169

Shortages Discovered After Opening the Boxes. Six American Manufacturers Were Deceived. The Reputation of Chinese Merchants Ruined by Bei Alone. Bei Xuehai, a native of Ningbo, previously operated the Baoyu Import and Export Firm in this city. He sold straw hat blanks to companies such as the Blumberg Company in New York, USA. However, after the goods arrived in New York, the buyers, together with local customs officials, opened the boxes for inspection and discovered that the goods inside were of much inferior quality compared to the samples. Furthermore, the number of items in each box was supposed to be 600, but only 300 were found. Therefore, the buyers believed that Baoyu had engaged in deceptive behavior and sent a telegram to Shanghai in January of this year to investigate. Bei Xuehai, seeing that his deception had been exposed, closed down the store and fled without a trace. It was not until May that Detective Feng Zhiming discovered that Bei was hiding in Fangbang Road in the city. He, together with the Public Security Bureau, rushed to arrest him and handed him over to the First Special District Local Court, which ordered the defendant to post bail pending further investigation. It is now learned that since November of last year, Bei has defrauded companies in New York out of a total of: $12,175.18 to the Openshaw Textile Company, $5,497.28 to the Hentze & Heymann, $8,321.17 to the Towro Lawson Brown, $5,086.88 to the A. Armitage, $13,128.38 to the Gemi, and $5,058.82 and $24,316.48 to the Blumberg Company in two separate incidents. The defrauded companies in New York have sent the samples and goods to Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, the police escorted Bei Xuehai to the court, where Judge Huang Risheng opened the trial. Police Lawyer Qian Xunjiu briefly described the case and presented the hat blanks of obviously superior and inferior quality as evidence. However, there are as many as six defrauded companies, and the court needs to investigate each one individually, which will take a considerable amount of time. Therefore, after questioning until 4:00 PM, the court ordered that the trial be adjourned to a later date.

Dysentery Outbreak in This City 170

Citizens Please Avoid Greed for Coolness Daily News Agency reports that at the time when true cholera was discovered in this city, dysentery was also discovered, but the situation was generally mild. Yesterday, a visit to the Red Cross Society's Epidemic Hospital on Tibet Road revealed that a large number of dysentery cases had suddenly been discovered in this city over the past week. At that time, more than 30 people went to the hospital for treatment every day. After five or six days, the number had decreased to about four or five people going to the hospital for treatment every day. The hospital is very careful in treating dysentery. However, statistics show that about three or four percent of the treated people died. The reason for the outbreak is that the weather is out of balance, and the weather is hot and cold. People who are greedy for coolness at night and drink unsanitary cold food are most susceptible to illness. The main cause of dysentery is excessive congestion. Therefore, it is hoped that citizens will pay attention to this.

Tongshang Bank Sues Dai Zhenwu for Debt Case 191

Full Text of the Japanese Consulate Judgment: Dai Loses and Provisional Execution Granted. Because Dai Zhenwu ignored the debt to Tongshang Bank, it led to the bank's chairman, Chuan Xiao'an, accusing lawyer Yan Dajue of conspiracy to intimidate. The Shanghai First Special District Court has scheduled a further hearing on the 7th. Regarding Dai Zhenwu's ignoring the debt, the Japanese Consulate has announced its judgment. The litigation costs are to be borne by the defendant, and provisional execution is granted. The judgment is recorded as follows: Judgment of the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai: Plaintiff: China Tongshang Bank, No. 7 Huangpu Bund, Shanghai, Legal Representative: Zhu Zikui, Litigation Agent: Lawyer Takada Ichiro. Defendant: Dai Zhenwu, No. 223 North Xizang Road, Shanghai, Litigation Agent: Lawyer Yano Nobuyuki. Between the above parties, regarding the loan recovery case No. 55 of the 9th year of Showa (1934), this Consulate General judges as follows: Main Text: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff principal of silver 73,000 taels and interest, of which (1) 50,000 taels, from January 25, Showa 8 (1933) until the date of repayment, at a monthly interest rate of 5%; (2) the remaining 23,000 taels, from January 25, Showa 8 (1933) until the date of repayment, at a monthly interest rate of 9%, compounded every three months. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. This judgment is subject to provisional execution. Facts: The plaintiff's agent requests a judgment as per items 1 and 2 of the main text, and requests a declaration of provisional execution. The statement briefly states that the plaintiff lent the defendant (A) 50,000 taels of silver on January 25, Showa 8 (1933), with a repayment date of six months, at a monthly interest rate of 9%; (B) 8,000 taels of silver; and (C) 15,000 taels of silver, all due for repayment on January 25, Showa 9 (1934), with a monthly interest rate of 9%, compounded every three months, with interest added to the principal. If the repayment is still not possible after the deadline, the amount of damages incurred according to the agreed interest rate will also be added to the principal silver every three months. Because the deadline has long passed and the defendant has not paid, this lawsuit is filed to demand repayment of the principal silver, agreed interest rate, and damages, etc., and the original document No. 1 (Dai's IOU) is presented as proof. Witness Zhu Huanwen is also requested for questioning. The witness claimed ignorance of document No. 1 of Yi (乙). The defendant's litigation agent requests the dismissal of the plaintiff's lawsuit and denies the fact asserted by the plaintiff regarding the loan of 50,000 taels. As for other facts, it is partially admitted, and it is argued that in September of Showa 6 (1931), Wang Xinguan, the manager of the plaintiff bank, had obtained the defendant's consent to borrow 50,000 taels of silver from the plaintiff in the defendant's name. However, there was no transfer of money between the two parties, so the contract cannot be established. Even if it is assumed to be established, Wang Xinguan was acting as an agent for both the plaintiff and the defendant when concluding the contract. This procedure violates Article 108 of the Civil Code and should be deemed invalid, etc., and document No. 1 of Yi (乙) is presented as proof. The defendant himself is also requested for questioning. The defendant fully admits the establishment of document No. 1 of Jia (甲). Reasons: The plaintiff lent the defendant 8,000 taels and 15,000 taels of silver on January 25, Showa 8 (1933), both with January 25, Showa 9 (1934) as the repayment date, at a monthly interest rate of 9%, compounded every three months, with interest added to the principal. The fact that after the repayment deadline, the damage amount according to the agreed interest rate is also added to the principal every three months has been admitted by the defendant and is therefore an undisputed fact. Regarding the plaintiff lending the defendant 50,000 taels of silver on January 25, Showa 8 (1933), with a monthly interest rate of 9%, and repayment of principal and interest after six months, combining document No. 1 of Jia (甲) (i.e., Dai's IOU) and the testimony of witness Zhu Huanzhi, this consulate finds the reasons for its establishment to be sufficient and without doubt. All documents No. 1 of Yi (乙) submitted by the defendant and the defendant's own statements are insufficient to influence the above finding. Therefore, this consulate considers the plaintiff's claim in this case based on the above facts to be entirely legitimate. Regarding the bearing of litigation costs, Article 89 of the Civil Procedure Law applies, and regarding the declaration of provisional execution, Article 196 of the same law applies. The judgment is as stated in the main text. Consul of the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai: Shimokawa Kuichi. Right Original Copy Without Error. July 30, Showa 9 (1934). Foreign Affairs Secretary of the same consulate: Kobayashi.

Preparation Report of China Industrial Bank 192

Open Letter to Comrades and Compatriots 199

Our party, with the Three Principles of the People as the national revolution, strives for the equality of the nation's political and economic status. For decades, we have never slacked off. Until the Northern Expedition in the 15th year of the Republic (1926), and then the establishment of the capital in Nanjing and the recovery of North China, the achievements were unexpected in less than two years. This is indeed because the doctrine of our party is sufficient to call on the masses, and the close cooperation of comrades and compatriots has enabled this great revolutionary cause to make considerable progress, and its achievements are also worthy of praise. Unfortunately, domestic rebels have risen repeatedly, and bandits and communists have been rampant. Natural disasters and man-made disasters have come one after another. When Japan took advantage of our suicidal situation, it seized our Northeast, invaded our Shanghai, seized our Rehe, and threatened our Pingjin. The party and the country are in danger of being toppled, and the nation has the pain of a gossamer thread. Our central government has handled it with caution, and Chairman Chiang has made various plans, so that the nation and the country can fortunately have a chance to rest and recuperate temporarily. However, the difficulty of our party's situation and the weight of responsibility will also increase day by day. Why? In terms of domestic politics, the realization of the Three Principles of the People must be based on whether the nation's political and economic status has been equalized. Therefore, the abolition of unequal treaties will make the nation-state tend towards prosperity and development to realize the principle of nationalism. The work of promoting local autonomy will enable the people to exercise political power and balance it with the government's governance power to realize the principle of democracy. The vigorous implementation of equal land rights and the control of capital will enable the people's livelihood problems to be universally resolved to realize the principle of people's livelihood. All these are necessary tasks in the revolutionary process. However, how much of these has our party started and how much has it completed? Thinking of this makes people sweat without being hot and shiver without being cold. Can all our comrades not realize the importance of their responsibilities and think of ways to serve themselves? Furthermore, let us try to talk about international politics. Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has despised international justice, destroyed the integrity of our national territory, and used all means to seize and plunder. The equilibrium situation in the Pacific has been broken by Japan's iron fist. In Europe, Germany and France are at odds, Italy and France are opposed, Germany and Russia are at odds, Britain and France are in conflict, and Britain, the United States, France, and Italy are vying for hegemony. The current situation in the Balkans has also returned to before 1914. The failure of the disarmament conference and the panic of the world economy have further increased the crisis. At this time, China, located in a sub-colony, has only two paths in front of it: one is to be slaughtered by imperialism and tend towards destruction, and the other is to work hard and strive for the revival of the nation. Where to go and what to do is up to our party to decide under China's current party-rule system. All responsibilities are borne by our party. Can our comrades not work hard? As described above, the responsibility of our party cannot be said to be insignificant. Therefore, our party considers the quantity and quality of party members, and is deeply worried that it will be insufficient to cope with national disasters and complete the revolution. The total population of the country is 470 million, and there are only more than 1.1 million party members, which is less than one-four-hundredth of the national population. Even in this city, with a population of 3 million, there are only more than 10,000 party members, accounting for about one-three-hundredth of the city's population. With this small number of party members leading the unorganized masses to complete such a large mission, even if everyone has three heads and six arms, it is feared that it will be difficult to achieve success. The truth is clear, and there is no need to avoid it. Moreover, (metabolism) allows all things to thrive. This law can also be applied to the organization of the party. If we listen to the gradual elimination of old members without new members to supplement them, then decades later, the party will not be a party, let alone a career, let alone a revolution. Our party deeply knows the necessity of absorbing new party members, and also knows that there are many outstanding elements outside the party who believe in the doctrine and are enthusiastic about the revolution, waiting for our party to accept them. Therefore, it is stipulated that 30,000 party members should be recruited in Shanghai, and this association will be responsible for it. It is also stipulated that each comrade must be responsible for introducing three new party members before September of this year to meet the predetermined number of 30,000 people. It is hoped that our comrades will find outstanding elements in their careers, social circles, groups, institutions, families, and relatives and friends, and sincerely invite them to join our party. With our comrades' usual loyalty and courage to the party, this work, which is of great importance and does not require much labor, will surely be completed quickly within the predetermined period. There is hope. Furthermore, this association also wants to inform our compatriots that human beings are political animals, and politics is the management of the affairs of the public. Since human beings cannot separate themselves from politics, human beings cannot but study politics, pay attention to politics, and participate in politics, and the organization of political parties has emerged accordingly. However, under China's current party-rule system, political power is in the hands of our party, and politics is guided by our party. The opportunity for the people to participate in actual politics is that in the near future, there is no other way than to join our party. Moreover, because the party is the party that exercises civil rights on behalf of the people, the fate of a country is largely tied to whether our party is sound. Therefore, if talented and capable people can join our party to contribute their abilities, not only can their political instincts be brought into play, but also helping our party is helping the entire China. Its significance is also very great. There were originally communist parties and so-called national socialist factions in the country. However, the Communist Party is kept and manipulated by Soviet Russia, and its nature is directly equal to that of Puyi, Japan's puppet, and the so-called Soviet in the red areas is also the same in form and substance as the puppet Manchukuo. How can we allow these traitors who sell themselves and forget their ancestors to seize the leadership of the Chinese revolution? As for the national socialists, although there was the organization of the Chinese Youth Party in the past, the party members are less than 1,000, the leaders have no ability, and their claims are all picked up from others and cannot form their own school. The misery of their present decline and the bleakness of their future can be judged without closing the coffin. Therefore, our party is not only the only large party in the country today, but it will also be the only large party in the country after handing over political power and disarming in the future. Therefore, for this very promising party, what concerns do our compatriots still have and why do they hesitate to move forward? Talented people, come on! Initiated by the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Kuomintang of China.

Reading News 201

Compiled by the Reading Guidance Department of the 申報 Circulation Library

Table of Contents 202

1. General Reading Life 2. Publication of Letter from the Author of "Six Soldiers" 3. Mail Forwarding

General Reading Life 203

Many readers are happy to know the reading life of people other than themselves. This is of great significance in exchanging personal reading life experiences. Because even if a hundred people read the same book, the results are rarely completely consistent because of the different reading lives of each person. Therefore, the experiences of others can not only be used as our reference, so that we can reduce some difficulties in the reading process, but also encourage us to move forward bravely and understand the hardships of learning. Therefore, things like reading experience talks have always been respected. Now let's talk about the general phenomenon of the reading life of our five or six hundred (limited to registered) readers! Naturally, we know it is still limited, but even based on the only materials we have received, we can extract the following important points, which are worth introducing in the Tao里. First, everyone is struggling for life while taking time out of their busy schedules to read. Life indicates their reading purpose and direction: and indicates the practical method of studying. They have gained many valuable experiences in this struggle, which cannot be obtained from books. Second, because reading can be based on the above practical experience of life as a starting point, the readers' progress is very rapid, and they often find answers to the difficult parts of the book in the practice of life. This phenomenon is not easy to see in school education. Third, they broke the pedantic atmosphere of (you must have a good environment to read). Because of the particularity of their respective lives, behind the counter of the store, in the workshop of the factory, when they were free, they wrote, in the public dormitory, in the park, on the tram, in the restaurant, they took out the books whenever they had time. They were able to make good use of the environment, overcome the environment, and repel all negative emotions. Fourth, they don't know a little then they have, once they know a little, they urgently demand to use it, as if they can't use the theory in the book, the book still can't be believed. Fifth, the more they read, the more dissatisfied they become, and the more and more complex the questions they ask us. Recently, Mr. Tuoluoqi wrote a thin book of questions to us. It can be seen that the readers' questions can only arise from (reading), and careless people can't even raise questions. In short: our readers are all moving forward on their own. In the past two months, it has been (sweating while reading intensely.)

Publishing the Letter from the Author of "Six Soldiers" 204

In the 20th issue of this magazine, an article by Lu Huo entitled (Special Issue on New Poetry Creation) was published. Now we have received a letter from the author of (Six Soldiers). The poem (Six Soldiers) is helpful. Mr. Lu Huo: After reading your article (Special Issue on (New Poetry) Creation), I would like to say a few words to you, because I am the author of (Six Soldiers). (Chorus Poetry) As soon as we see this thing, we will understand that it is imported. It is said to be popular in Europe and the United States, but what I have seen is written by workers. I don't know if there are any written by soldiers. In China, I heard that Mr. Yang Sao has written it? Whether the result is a failure or a success, no one knows, because few people know where he published it. After (Six Soldiers), I wrote...Two Brothers, Defend Russia, Wake Up, Manchuria! (These things may be accumulated together and meet the world, but I dare not say it now.) They all failed, and the reason is as Mr. said (there are many places that cannot be sung together, and singing is not tense, incomprehensible, and the words spoken by many characters must be introduced like a play.) Why is this? My experience is this: For example, Goer德's (120 Million), only a rectangular table is enough. But the setting for writing about soldiers is different. First of all, it is not easy to perform; especially in China, it is difficult to write things. Originally, I wanted to write this poem from three aspects: the war scene, the officers, and the soldiers, but the result is that only the last bit can become a (?) chorus, and the first two major paragraphs have become a burden. This really has to be said to be (defeating its purpose)! The few poems written later have been partially improved, but the material is still soldiers, so it is another failure. To tell the new comers about my failure, (I hope (Six Soldiers) can do a little bit of (introducing jade by throwing brick). If you are not absolutely necessary, please do not take the material from the soldiers, because this is extremely difficult to write well. Of course, there are many things that can be taken from. In terms of form, I think that the minimum limit is that Europeization should be avoided, because the writer is Chinese and the reader is also Chinese. It is necessary to make one's own work an antidote to the reader's pain. I believe that a nation has its unique characteristics, that is to say, the form may be national. The dialogue written in is best written by the author and then ask a few friends to sing it on the spot, and modify the inappropriate places immediately. This may become a perfect mass chorus poem. The above are my opinions. I hope you can publish the letter. Dou Yinfu

Free Talk

The Necessity of Europeanization in Literary Language 206

— Long Gonggong

I am not accusing Mr. Wen Gongzhi of pretending to be a representative, directly advocating for Mr. (Combert), and secretly intending to promote Western aggression. However, I fully agree with the idea of (adding some Europeanization to Chinese grammar). Especially in translation and creative writing, for the sake of (precision and accuracy), the Europeanization of vocabulary and grammar is absolutely necessary.

A certain gentleman once said that the strength of classical Chinese lies in its vagueness and ambiguity, which is true. Vernacular Chinese is more (precise and accurate) than classical Chinese, so the proportion of Europeanization cannot but be greater. Popular language is even more (precise and accurate) than vernacular Chinese, so there is no doubt that Chinese grammar will become even more Europeanized in the future.

In fact, the Europeanization of Chinese grammar did not begin with the emergence of vernacular Chinese or Mr. Combert's advocacy. There were (opium "pilisuon") in Liang Qichao's classical Chinese writings. Before him, (Sanskrit) was commonly used in ancient texts. And for the machine workers in Guangdong, words like (spare), (spiral), and (switch) have become part of their daily language for the past twenty years. These people may not necessarily be (directed by imperialists), so why does Mr. Wen only blame Mr. Combert?

Most of the current literary works in China are a kind of game of vague and ambiguous concepts. Very few can concretely describe a chair or finely portray an action. They almost completely lack the ability to create images with language. This is probably due to the excessive number of people whose thoughts are similar to Mr. Wen Gongzhi. However, once exposed to Western literature, even literal translations cannot lack Europeanized vocabulary and grammar. Can China hope to produce great works?

The basic skill of Europeanization is the use of punctuation, which is a well-known fact. However, even this necessary basic skill is quite difficult to master. For example, if you put a question mark after the sentence (I really don't know where to start), it would be considered an error. Mr. Wen Gongzhi has not advocated abolishing punctuation marks, and he uses them himself, so it seems that (necessity) is beyond doubt. However, even this small point has not been understood, which shows that although Chinese people may be useful, they cannot necessarily speak well.

Gorky could speak, and spoke very well. He described a (failed writer). Let me copy two sentences for everyone to see:

(The young man, as he spoke, twisted the sparse and lusterless hairs on his upper lip with his mouth, half-closed his melancholy, yellowish-white eyes, and very carefully poured himself a glass of vodka with a trembling hand.)

(...His loose cheeks were covered with red streaks formed by many small veins, and his nose was poisoned by alcohol, turning chestnut-colored, drooping above his upper lip in a miserable way.) (Random Recollections: Page 75)

From these two examples, anyone can see the poverty of Chinese vocabulary and the incompleteness of grammar. However, it is entirely due to the Europeanization of those sentences that they can convey a few percent of the characters Gorky wanted to describe. Who would be willing to rewrite those two sentences using (pure Chinese vocabulary and grammar)? They would then know that the true intention of the imperialists is probably to have Chinese people use (classical Chinese) entirely. If one only has a vague and ambiguous concept of everything, one will naturally not be able to speak clearly about the imperialists' acts of aggression.

The Issue of Europeanization 207

— Xian He

Now is the time when the discussion of popular language is at its peak. There are already many articles against classical Chinese, but very few discussing the issue of Europeanization.

A few days ago, I saw Mr. Combert's (joke, just treat it as a joke), which touched upon this issue. This is naturally valuable, but because the argument is ambiguous, it can easily cause misunderstandings.

My biggest regret is that Mr. Combert treats the serious matter of attacking Europeanized vernacular Chinese as just a joke. But in fact, it is definitely not like that.

I think it is right to oppose Europeanization, because what the public can understand is definitely not the difficult and obscure Europeanized vernacular Chinese. A characteristic of foreign languages is that there are many descriptive words. Often, to describe a simple thing, a series of adjectives is needed. This is of course (precise), as Mr. Combert said, but if it is imitated improperly or excessively, it becomes (cluttered). In foreign languages themselves, it is of course a progressive thing, because it can express more complex thoughts and feelings. But after Chinese writers imitate it, it becomes a pile of rubbish that does not make sense. Now, no matter which literary book on the market you open, it is often full of long sentences, with some inappropriate or even incoherent "de" characters in between. Needless to say, this is the result of deliberate imitation. Especially the fourteen-line poems in new poetry, which are simply upside down and装得異常古怪 (decorated extraordinarily strange), even college students majoring in literature will not understand. The reason for this phenomenon is mostly due to the authors' curiosity and blind worship of foreign things, and not because the inherent vernacular Chinese is not enough. In fact, it is a very superficial and ordinary thing, but they insist on pulling on a bright and dazzling foreign tiger skin in an attempt to cover up ugliness, resulting in incoherence or awkwardness. Is this also the (precision) that Mr. Combert wants to promote?

The most important thing is to strictly distinguish between (mysterious) and (cluttered). We demand clear and fluent writing to match substantial content, but we oppose the rambling and verbose Europeanized vernacular Chinese. Of course, I am not saying that we absolutely cannot adopt modern European and American literary styles, but I am attacking the new-style formalistic writing that is currently popular, which is forcibly imitated by general writers and scholars without being assimilated.

Moreover, what I am referring to here is creative writing. Translation should be more tolerant. However, it is naturally more desirable to be able to translate (foreign languages) with (Chinese), rather than translating (real European languages) with (disguised European languages). At a time when the level of cultural education is very low and the public is already yearning for knowledge, I believe that easy understanding is the first element. If a piece of material that is originally easy to understand is blurred by difficult and obscure writing, it is undoubtedly a sin. Translation should of course be faithful, and should not be arbitrarily changed or deleted, but striving for fluency and conciseness is an important condition, and it is also possible in practice. For example, Mr. Cao Jinghua's translation of (Andrei's Wrong Path) is very smooth and is a powerful example.

As for Mr. Combert's examples of place names, such as (Avenue Joffre) and (Avenue des Soeurs), to defend the necessity of Europeanization, I think it is ridiculous, because this is not (precision) at all. In the current creative writing circle, trendy authors always love to fill in a batch of foreign names, thinking that this is complex and new, making it neither fish nor fowl. Is using glamorous names like (Louise), (Manly), and (Nana) to replace (Little Cat), (Emerald), and (Shi Chai) what Mr. Combert calls (precision)?

In short, I strongly oppose the currently popular formalistic vernacular Chinese, because it is alienated from the people and is a form forcibly copied by intellectuals without digestion. But I definitely do not completely deny the role of modern European and American literary styles in helping to establish a popular language, or stubbornly uphold national essence like conservative gentlemen. Therefore, my fundamental proposition is: to (abandon) the (Europeanized vernacular Chinese).

From Beyond the Horizon 208

— Lin Xi

Why do you always walk silently up this silent slope, facing the setting sun? Whenever the setting sun lengthens the shadows of the trees, I always see you gazing wistfully towards the horizon.

The flock of sheep at the foot of the slope knows: the front of the slope was originally covered with continuous green grass. Now that green grass has been trampled by you into a path, and you always linger silently on that path.

Could it be that the setting sun has brought news again - unfortunate? Could it be that the vastness of the distant trees has stirred up your memories? But seeing the floating clouds, you should be vigilant, right? Why are you still walking, walking, silently?

On Physiognomy 209

— Zhuan Zhai

Everyone has a face, but unless you have (read many people) or learned some Ma Yi physiognomy, it is difficult to distinguish between good and bad, good and evil. Legend has it that Yuan Tiangang was good at physiognomy, but he looked at Li Qiao's face for three days and three nights before reaching a conclusion. This shows how profound a (science) it is.

The West is worthy of worship. In the early 19th century, a type of phrenology was popular, which was roughly similar to our country's (bone reading physiognomy). China has sent students to study abroad for many years, but so far, no one has introduced such a science, which is as beautiful as (scientific spiritualism). This shows how bad the students studying abroad are.

However, with the popularity of newspapers and magazines, the advancement of photography and industry, portraits of famous people at home and abroad are reflected in our eyes, and most of them are shocking to the eye. So that's what they look like! Because of the different races, Eastern and Western people have two completely different faces, and each has its own views on beauty and ugliness, right? By carefully observing their appearance, it is not difficult to understand what kind of soul is contained within the skin.

However, when looking at Westerners, whether they are political leaders, movie stars, writers, philosophers... or the like, whether they are serious or unrestrained, you can roughly see traces of struggle. They have a distinct appearance. Even in terms of political figures, Briand's ugly face, Mussolini's round fat man, Stalin's big nose, and Hitler's sad eyebrows all seem to have a kind of characteristic that makes people not feel vague. Whether they are smart or stupid, cunning or straightforward, their expressions are ultimately obvious. Only MacDonald is a little off, but his hypocrisy is obvious, and he is still in the category of being clear.

However, when compared with our country's big and small figures, celebrities and dignitaries, it is really incomparable. This aspect is a blurred image. Not only can outsiders not see anything, but it seems that even they themselves hate that face. When photographed in films, most of them look like they are smiling but frowning, like anger and joy, seemingly serious but also humorous, seemingly merciful but also ferocious, like floating smoke, looming.

(Merely having the appearance) is not possible, which is enough to see the emptiness of the content. The Japanese of the same race are much different, but their appearance sometimes seems to be acting, and their expressions seem to be excessive.

Tracing the History of Popular Language Literature (Part 1) 210

— Yu Shixia

The author has briefly discussed ancient popular language literature in the August 10 issue of this publication. For the sake of thoroughness, this article is also written. Ancient popular language literature is naturally not limited to poetry.

The chapter novels since the Yuan and Ming dynasties still inherited the tradition of storytellers. They wrote in the popular language of the time, simply to make the public able to say it, understand it, and see it clearly. *Water Margin*, *Journey to the West*, and *Golden Lotus* are such things.

The origin of *ci* poetry may be related to the songs of the streets and alleys of the common people, but once it enters the hall of elegance, it becomes the exclusive possession of a special group, because only they have the enjoyment of fine wine, women, and singing. There are places with 并水飤 (merging water and feed), and there are people singing Liu Yong's lyrics. I remember that this was the impression gained from an envoy of an enemy country in the Song Dynasty, perhaps referring to the city. Now Liu Yong's lyrics are still there, but they are not necessarily the things of the common people. Even if it is spread to the public, it is like songs like Taohuajiang drizzle, which are popular among rickshaw pullers, but only because they are accustomed to hearing them. However, the real enjoyers of such songs are ultimately another special group. Some literary historians think that *ci* poetry is popular literature, which is extremely ridiculous!

Now I want to talk about drama.

We are not very clear about the dance postures of the early people and the situation of ancient witchcraft dances. From the village exorcism ceremony (鄉人儺) revered by Confucius to the present-day welcoming gods and thanking the gods, this superstitious, barbaric religious ritual has some theatrical meaning and has been related to the development and evolution of drama in history. The *jiao di* (wrestling) of the Qin and Han dynasties, up to the *bai xi* (hundred entertainments) of the Sui and Tang dynasties, in addition to the meaning of entertaining monarchs and bureaucrats, also contained the meaning of showing off authority. In terms of foreign affairs, this could intimidate the surrounding barbarians. The reason why Emperor Wu of Han and Emperor Yang of Sui held *jiao di* and *bai xi* to entertain the barbarian envoys and merchants who came to surrender was this. In terms of internal affairs, this could intimidate the people, let the common people see power, and at the same time entertain them and vent their grievances. This meaning also existed. What's more, this kind of performance originally had the meaning of scaring ghosts, driving away epidemics, entertaining gods, and praying for the year, we can also sense it! In short, the reason why drama arose was due to the contribution of many factors, and it was definitely not just for the entertainment of the public. This is what we should know.

The *da qu* (grand songs), *can jun* (attendant officer dramas), and *guan ben za ju* (official script miscellaneous dramas) of the Tang and Song dynasties were mostly the things of the Jiaofang musicians, serving the court, which had nothing to do with the public. The *yuan ben* (academy scripts) and *za ju* (miscellaneous dramas) of the Jin and Yuan dynasties naturally evolved from these things. It is difficult to investigate what *yuan ben* were like. Judging from the name, since it is the foundation of the brothels, the things popular in the brothels, it should have had the opportunity to be close to the public. Furthermore, *za ju* seems to be a bit different from the later *chuan qi* (legends), which almost completely became a kind of performance for a special group. At least its tunes and dialogue were much more popular and did not intentionally focus on rhetoric and parallelism. However, according to the records we have already found, the performance of *za ju* and *chuan qi* was by Jiaofang actors. It is still doubtful whether there were folk troupes.

Pihuang arose after *chuan qi*, although promoted by a special group, it was related to the public. Not only were its tunes and dialogue using languages and words that were closer to the public, but also such troupes were found in major cities and towns throughout the country, and even in rural market towns. Therefore, we want to say that Beijing opera is an art that is appreciated by both the elegant and the popular.

Old Man (3) 211

— Jin Yi

But in his eyes, everything was beautiful, and every object had a glorious past. Apart from those that he had used himself or that belonged to his family, those that were sold to him by others (this was also five years ago, and in the five years he did not have the money to buy other people's old things) also had their own stories, which the sellers told him with tears in their eyes. At that time, he might also shed some tears, stuff the money into the seller's hand, listen to his thanks, and walk out, leaving this broken thing here. Turning around, he would feel cheated and get angry, scolding his only assistant (this assistant was his grandson, whose name was Alexander, usually called Sasha for short, a young man in his twenties).

He moved to the side. But he clearly imprinted that beautiful story in his mind, and if a customer took a fancy to it, he could tell the story even more movingly, in order to get a good price.

(You must not wrinkle your brow when you see that it is broken, it is a top-quality product made in our Russia. -- But not the current Russia, that group of rebellious countries. This accordion was used by a singer who caused a sensation throughout St. Petersburg in 1851, maybe 52, called something No --, you must forgive me, I can't remember, I am almost seventy years old. -- It was used by him. You must know that this No -- was young and beautiful, and many women were obsessed with him, but he had a bad temper and didn't like those girls. I know that some women who couldn't get close to him bribed his servants to secretly kiss his accordion. If you don't believe me, smell it and see, there is still the fragrance of face powder! He fell in love with a woman who didn't love him at all, and things in the world are so strange. He never got her favor in his life, so he took his piano and jumped into the river and died--)

He warmed the story of this broken accordion in his heart, and a difficulty arose, that is, would saying that its owner committed suicide scare the buyers a little?

But this story made him very satisfied, and even he himself was deceived. He laboriously brought his nose close to the accordion to smell whether there was a fragrance of face powder.

Secondary Education

Recent Reforms (Middle)

- A Conversation with Officials in Charge of the Ministry of Education - (3) The Problem of the Secondary School Graduation Examination In order to standardize the graduation level of students and improve teaching efficiency, the Ministry issued the Provisional Regulations for the Secondary and Primary School Student Graduation Examination in May of the 21st year of the Republic of China. At the end of the first semester of the 21st year, Hunan, Guangxi, and Shandong rushed to hold it. By the end of the second semester, 18 provinces and cities had held it. In order to gather opinions and improve the examination methods, the Ministry sent out a questionnaire regarding the graduation examination at the beginning of the 22nd year to solicit opinions from all parties. A total of 17 provinces and cities replied and compiled the responses as a reference for revising the previous regulations. In December of the 22nd year, the Secondary School Student Graduation Regulations were promulgated, and the Provisional Regulations were abolished. The Ministry again compiled a booklet of statistics on the graduation examinations for secondary and primary school students in various provinces and cities in the 21st year based on the numerical statistics of the questionnaire answers and issued it to the education departments of various provinces and cities to show the best and worst subjects in the 21st year graduation examination, as well as the reasons and remedial methods. The subjects with relatively poor graduation examination results for secondary and primary school students were mathematics and natural science. Therefore, in addition to instructing the relevant departments to earnestly improve, it was stipulated that public and private universities should hold outlines for summer training classes for science teachers in secondary schools and asked the universities to follow them in order to remedy the situation. This summer vacation, the universities have already followed the order to hold them. The secondary school student graduation examination this summer vacation was held uniformly throughout the country, and the results have improved compared to the past. The Ministry has again issued an order to the relevant departments that schools with poor examination results should be warned by the competent education administrative organs and ordered to improve. Those with poor results that are difficult to improve should be ordered to close in order to avoid harming young people. The social bureaus of Beiping and Nanjing have already implemented this, and the remaining departments are also successively complying. Since the Ministry implemented the Provisional Regulations for the Secondary and Primary School Student Graduation Examination to the present, all universities have been instructed to pay special attention when enrolling new students. Those applicants whose secondary school graduation certificates do not have the words "passed the examination" or do not have a certificate of qualification for admission to higher education issued by the competent education administrative organ are generally not allowed to register for the examination. Since the implementation of the graduation examination, people in various places have mostly agreed with the examination in principle, but have criticized the examination regulations and other related issues. After carefully translating various criticisms, there are some misunderstandings. I will briefly describe them below. (A) The Problem of Textbooks As a result of the secondary school student graduation examination in Hebei and other provinces this year, nearly three-tenths or one-third of the students failed. There are many reasons for this, and some argue that the lack of uniformity in the textbooks used by various schools is a major reason. However, the examination questions issued by the education departments of various provinces and cities are based on the secondary school curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry, and the textbooks of various publishing houses must be edited according to these standards. After being reviewed and approved by the Ministry, schools may adopt them. According to the law, schools must not adopt textbooks and books that have not been approved. However, in practice, schools still inevitably violate this. Before there were graduation examination measures, the drawbacks were still hidden. Once the examination was held, the drawbacks were immediately revealed. In the future, if the Ministry's review of textbooks is stricter and the examination of teaching materials by local education administrative organs is stricter, the drawbacks pointed out by the critics can be completely eliminated. Second Sea Crossing Competition 226

▲Held on the 19th Shanghai Gaoqiao Beach, in order to enhance the interest in the sea, created the first 2,000-meter sea crossing competition last year. Although the wind and waves were strong at that time, and the boats could not bear the gaze of the audience, the participants still bravely moved forward. Sure enough, the results were excellent. Looking at the follow-up of this year's capital and Hangzhou ferry crossing competitions, it is enough to arouse a lot of interest in water sports. At the height of the swimming season, the second sea crossing competition is scheduled to be held at 10:00 AM on the 19th, with six lifeboats and 24 lifebuoys to protect water safety. In terms of prizes, requests have been made to Mayor Wu and various bureau chiefs and celebrities at sea to award them to the winners. It is hoped that maritime athletes will participate as soon as possible. The registration office is located at No. 70 Cichang Lane, Nanjing Road. Little Football Club Begins Registration 227

The Municipal First Sports Ground has been creating small football sports for ten years, promoting them across the country. The venue also holds a small football competition once a year to promote it. It is heard that the ninth small football competition began registration yesterday, which is generally the same as the previous one, and is still divided into four groups: Strong Men, Youth, Athletes, and Young Friends. However, in order to enhance sportsmanship, the registration for the Strong Men group is more restricted. All teams and players who have defaulted twice before, or have committed insulting referees, hating opponents, or exhibiting barbaric behavior, are not allowed to participate. The registration deadline is September for the Strong Men group and September 9 for the Youth, Athletes, and Young Friends groups.

Yang Hsiu-chiung's Inscription for Luen Wah Woolen Mill 231

Miss Yang Hsiu-chiung returned to Hong Kong from Shanghai the day before yesterday. Her father and Mr. Chen Tso-chien, a prominent figure in the local knitting industry, were fellow villagers. It was immediately handed over to Mr. Chen as a memento.

Gold and Silver Prices May Rise to One Dollar 232

Gold Speculation Plummets by Eleven and a Half Dollars 233

▲Swap Discount Suddenly Drops to Three Dollars and Fifty Cents▲ The gold market experienced another decline yesterday. The overall trend was still flat, but the swap discount suddenly plummeted. Favorable news about silver led to active selling. Initially, overseas silver markets saw London rising and the U.S. remaining flat. London spot gold increased by half a penny, and exchange rates rose significantly. U.S. cotton fell by 20 points, and U.S. wheat decreased by 1/8 of a cent. As a result, sentiment remained relatively stable. Raw material trading opened with a slight decrease to $56. Gold businesses anticipated lower trading volumes. After the opening, due to bank tightness and abundant exchange rates, HSBC quoted British rates as flat and U.S. rates up by 1/8 of a cent. Settlement prices continued to approach, and the gold market declined. However, it managed to maintain some level after the drop. Therefore, the situation was highly volatile in the middle of the day. Eventually, there was a slight source of spot goods in the market, but spot dealers had no appetite. The swap discount suddenly dropped, affecting sentiment and creating a downward trend. Due to the strengthening of the exchange market, selling was more prevalent, leading to a further decline. However, there was fierce struggle at the $50 mark, making it extremely difficult to predict the market direction. Later, a private cable from New Fuhong Trading Company stated that the U.S. government had decided to purchase large quantities of silver abroad, with the possibility of silver prices rising to one dollar. Selling intensified, and other foreign firms also received similar messages. Gold prices then retreated below $50, showing a sudden weakness. The market became hesitant after Western brokers dumped December U.S. dollars at $36, but struggled. Afterwards, the domestic market strengthened, with December U.S. dollars rising above $36. The market followed suit and declined. Finally, news from Bombay reported only a one-anna increase, halting the selling momentum. Buyers were willing to become active at the lower prices, gradually pulling the market up. The situation remained uncertain. The price of pure gold was $969.10. There was a slight source of spot goods, but the lack of interest from buyers led to a sudden drop in the swap discount to $3.50, which significantly impacted sentiment. Grains

Amidst a Frenzy of Falling Foreign Wheat Prices

Futures Flour Collapses 245

▲October Futures Break Through the 0.6 Yuan Mark▲

Yesterday, the flour market experienced a rare and violent decline in all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat quotes from Chicago fell by about 1.67 yuan, and Canadian wheat fell by a huge 2.23 yuan. The market sentiment had already been wavering in the previous week due to the gradual increase in factory inventory. Declines had been frequent, suggesting a possible rebound. However, with the sharp fall in foreign wheat prices, the price of spot foreign wheat, though not determined by local factories due to tariffs, was easily set by factories in Shandong Province, which were not bound by such restrictions. Due to these concerns, market sentiment turned sharply negative. The opening price for the current month fell to 0.61 yuan, a significant drop of 0.15 yuan compared to the previous week's closing price. Prices for subsequent months also fell by 0.1 yuan. However, after the sharp decline, short sellers rushed to cover, and the market rebounded slightly, rising by 0.05 to 0.06 yuan in the first session. In the afternoon, the situation looked grim. The degree of the fall resembled the frenzy of a rise, because various factories pushed down the prices, while most of the bullish traders were outsiders, so they had no power to resist the headwind. As a result, the opening price for the current month fell sharply again by 0.06 to 0.07 yuan, and prices for September and October also plummeted simultaneously. Prices for August, September, and October all fell below the 0.6 yuan mark, a difference of more than 0.3 yuan compared to the highest market value at the beginning of the previous week. Although such a rapid rise and fall each had its basis, careful consideration suggests that they were not realistic and seemed to have a cause-and-effect relationship. As a result, the current month fell by a staggering 0.175 yuan compared to the previous week, September fell by 0.1825 yuan, October fell by 0.185 yuan, November fell by 0.1775 yuan, December fell by 0.1625 yuan, and January fell by 0.1525 yuan. The total transaction volume for the day reached over 1.8 million bags.

The wheat futures market experienced an unprecedented plunge.

October Futures Fall by as Much as 0.8 Yuan from the Highest Point 246

Yesterday, the wheat futures market saw a sharp decline across all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat quotes from Chicago fell by about 1.67 yuan, and Canadian wheat fell by about 2.23 yuan. With the adverse turn of events abroad, domestic grain prices also turned from their peak. Yesterday's sharp fall in foreign wheat prices greatly impacted the sentiment of both industry insiders and outsiders. Opening prices for near and distant months fell sharply by about 0.2 yuan compared to the previous week, and by as much as 0.25 yuan for distant months. The closing price rebounded slightly as the trend became clearer. In the afternoon, due to the instability in the flour market and the possibility of approaching pricing for imported wheat, market sentiment changed again, and prices for all months plunged again. Most amateur bullish traders also rushed to sell. The magnitude of the fall set a new record since the exchange was established. In the end, compared to the highest record on the 8th of this month, the current month fell by 0.58 yuan, September fell by 0.55 yuan, October fell the most by 0.7 yuan, November fell to 0.6 yuan, and December fell to 0.54 yuan. Compared to the previous week's closing price, the current month fell by 0.33 yuan, September fell by 0.37 yuan, October fell by 0.35 yuan, November fell by 0.41 yuan, and December fell by 0.36 yuan. In the spot wheat market, factories unanimously rejected purchases, and while the market called for 4 yuan, factories showed no interest.

Other oils and peanut oil also saw sharp declines, with buyers temporarily sticking to lower bids.

Due to the decline in cake sales, factories were inactive with regards to old yellow soybeans, and continuous small telegrams led to depreciation and decline. Yesterday's selling price had to be lowered by a fraction compared to last weekend. Five to six cartloads of various beans were traded, all in small quantities. On average, each yuan in national currency could be sold for 16.6875 to 16.75 pence. As a result, the cost of imported woolen fabrics was somewhat reduced. Previously, each yuan in customs duties required 2 yuan plus some change in foreign currency, but now it only requires 1.93 yuan. Thus, the average import duty per box could be reduced by more than 20 yuan compared to before.

Spring and Autumn

Records of Lingering Fragrance from the Emperor’s Past 251

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

However, while I was secretly worried alone, the rest of the female officials, palace maids, and eunuchs did not seem to have any feelings. They only knew that a small incident had occurred, that the Empress Dowager's beloved antiques and jade artifacts had fallen. They reacted as ordinary people would to such an event, rushing forward to quickly pick up what had already fallen and support what was about to fall, almost everyone exerting all their strength. But this commotion threw the small court on the train into complete disorder and chaos. In the palace or in the Summer Palace, it could be said that such a loss of composure had never happened in hundreds of years! If those courtiers who had previously desperately petitioned against the Empress Dowager's risky train ride to Fengtian had seen this scene, they would surely shake their heads and stamp their feet, lamenting: (Could we have advised against it? Now you see, isn't this an ominous omen)?

Because I had already accepted that the situation was beyond repair, and perhaps because I was simply terrified, I stood by with my hands in my sleeves, hoping that the Empress Dowager herself would come up with a good way to remedy the situation. But she didn't say a word. I couldn't help but turn my head and glance at her—with great fear in my heart—but to my surprise, she was smiling gently. At such a time, that she could not only remain calm but also give us a warm smile was truly a rare event! A great weight lifted from my heart. But I was so scared that I almost fell. My legs were trembling uncontrollably, and my hands were as cold as winter. I thought that if everyone were as scared as I was, standing frozen and just watching those things fall and break, we would inevitably suffer a terrible ordeal. Fortunately, they forgot the dignity of the court and acted in such a hurried and chaotic manner, which made the Empress Dowager turn anger into laughter and turn a major event into nothing. It was truly a great stroke of luck amidst misfortune! (104)

Entrance Examinations During the Summer Vacation 252

— Mei Xue

These past few days have been truly difficult for me. Holding my high school diploma, I rushed to Shanghai to take the university entrance exams. In the sweltering heat, we battled in the examination hall. Universal balm and *bagua dan* pills were our essential medicines for this "civil service exam." Under the pressure of "hot," "extreme," and "suffocating," we were either drenched in sweat or so anxious that our faces turned pale as paper. I can't produce any sophisticated writing, so I'll just adapt two of Wang Bo's famous lines to describe us exam-takers: "(Sweat and ink fly together, faces and paper share the same color)." Of course, I couldn't be excluded from the exam-takers.

(A cunning rabbit has three burrows.) Taking university entrance exams is the same; there is little hope if you only apply to one school. All of us taking the entrance exams had to apply to at least three universities, and I was no exception. I took exams for Tsinghua, Jiaotong, and Zhejiang universities, fulfilling the saying "(Rising from three exams)." When taking the Tsinghua exam, describing the face of a beggar was difficult for me. When taking the Jiaotong exam, mistakenly building a Shaanxi house was difficult for me. When taking the Zhejiang exam, my whole back was sore, which was difficult for me.

When taking the Tsinghua exam, the science questions weren't particularly difficult, but the English questions were truly unbearable. The other examinees were also staring blankly, pens in hand. I was one of those staring blankly. The general meaning of the question was: "(If a beggar asks you for money, what does the beggar's face look like before you give him money? What does the beggar's face look like after you give him money? Describe the two appearances of the beggar in no more than 150 words.)" Heavens! How could I describe a beggar's face in 150 words? I wish I could grab a vagrant and experiment on him in real time!

When taking the Jiaotong exam, there was a question in the general knowledge section that required translating a classical Chinese phrase into modern Chinese: "(Qin had no *lu*, not because there were no *lu*, but because everyone could make *lu*)." At first glance, translating these few words seemed effortless. I immediately wrote down (Shaanxi had no houses, not because there were no houses, but because everyone could build houses.) I thought I was probably correct. After leaving the exam hall, I told my teacher, Lao Jia, who laughed and said: "(You're mistaken. The original text comes from the *Kaogong Ji* in the *Zhouli Dongguan*. The character *lu* doesn't mean house; it refers to the shaft of a spear or halberd.)" When I heard this, I was initially disappointed, then amused. That day, I wasn't the only one who mistakenly built a Shaanxi house. Probably 99 out of 100 people were confused by the two meanings.

When taking the Zhejiang exam, the questions weren't difficult, but the seats were too cramped. I took the exam for three days, and my back ached for three days.

Each time I took an exam, I had to undergo a physical examination. I weighed 105 pounds for the first exam, lost one pound for the second exam, and lost another half pound for the third exam. (Doesn't see an ounce of meat, the same when taking the exam.)

Difficulty of Going Abroad 253

— Cape Prisoner

Foreigners coming to China have always been as if entering an unpopulated land, our customs officials greet them with open arms. Chinese people, on the other hand, not only endure all sorts of hardships and bitterness when residing abroad, such as in colonies, but even taking a single step outside the country's borders has recently become as difficult as (the road to Shu).

(Nanyang), for hundreds of years, has always been like the outer prefecture of our Fujian and Guangdong provinces. Annam, Siam, Burma, British Malaya, American Philippines, Dutch East Indies... These places? Our overseas Chinese population numbers in the tens of thousands in some places and in the millions in others, far exceeding the number of white residents of the ruling countries. The development and prosperity of these places have largely been fueled by the blood and sweat of overseas Chinese. However, now, in order to limit Chinese people, the colonial governments only allow you to return, not to enter, creating a situation of (being able to leave but not to return).

Recently, a friend responded to an invitation from an overseas Chinese school in Singapore. Anxious to get to the opening of the school, he hastily set off, obtained a passport, paid the ten yuan entrance tax, had it signed by the British Consul in Shanghai, and went to buy a ship ticket. Singapore! Only a few steps outside our South Gate! But you have to take a foreign ship. Each ship is limited to carrying fifteen Chinese to Nanyang, and tickets are sold out well in advance. Although there are many empty cabins on board, they would rather transport air. My friend was impatient and heard people say that there were more ships available in Hong Kong. So he bought a ticket to Hong Kong first. Unexpectedly, when he arrived in Hong Kong, he learned that there were dozens of times more people waiting for ships to Nanyang than in Shanghai. Some had been waiting in hotels for more than half a month. The hotels were raising the price of ship tickets like stocks with triple the dividends. After waiting for more than ten days and going through many twists and turns, he finally scraped together a high-priced third-class ticket and set off towards the scorching equator. It is still unknown whether the journey ahead will be smooth. Now, new arrivals to the Dutch East Indies have to pay an import tax of more than 300 yuan in national currency, and those going to the Philippines have to pay more than 1,000 yuan in Philippine currency (?). Poor Chinese people don't even have a share in going abroad to find a loaf of bread!
