Old Woman Wang 256

— Ma Ying

Our neighbor has an old woman who is already in her sixties this year. Her maiden name is probably only known to herself, because her married name is Wang, so everyone calls her Old Woman Wang.

We are not very familiar with Old Woman Wang's history, but we heard the elders talking: she was widowed three years after she married, and she vowed to remain chaste. At that time, she was only twenty years old. It is indeed very rare for such a young woman to have such a strong concept of chastity.

She endured hunger and cold, working alone, resting alone, only her shadow was her companion.

It is said that in the first year of her widowhood, she did not speak a word to any strange man except for a few close elders.

At that time, the forces of old ethics were particularly strong in the countryside. Old Woman Wang's act of living a solitary and bitter life to maintain chastity for her husband had long been respected by the respectable people. But on the other hand, the so-called petty vagrants and idlers in the countryside, like swarms of bees and butterflies, gathered all their strength to attack her.

In the spring of the second year, flowers sprouted, grass grew fragrant, swallows chirped, and butterflies danced in pairs. That light, intoxicating spring air entered the hearts of every young man and woman, as if they were mesmerized. Old Woman Wang at this time! At that time, she was only twenty-one years old, don't be misled by the word "old"! Her actions suddenly changed. One night in March, something unexpected happened: Old Woman Wang, under the threat of a man, in the nick of time, suddenly felt a chill in her heart, violently pushed the man away, fled out the door, and finally threw herself into the river. Fortunately, she was rescued and did not lose her life.

After that, she would avoid men from a distance when she saw them. It is still like this now. But now she is old. Sometimes, sitting in front of the door, she looks up at the sky, and a lonely sadness seems to be hidden in the wrinkles on her face.

Small Parts 257

— (Xin Ren)

Because humans have a strong love of beauty, often having a small scar on the face will lead to a lifetime of unhappiness, or be considered a lifelong regret. But our clever ladies will use beautiful hair to cover the defects of the face, at the same time, just like wearing dark glasses because of a blind eye, which leads to more inconvenience.

Acting cute and coquettish is the most effective husband-managing technique for ladies, but it also depends on the occasion. Sometimes it will lead to annoyance and two slaps in the face.

If you want to climb up to a famous dancer, you will see many cold looks from her. At the same time, everything about this dancer is not necessarily that good. If you want to climb up to a dancer whose business is slow, you can not only save money, but also get more benefits. There is a lot to be said about spending the same amount of money, so you must be careful.

Doctor of Quality Studies 258

— Chen Jingyu

Old friend Mr. Tong came from the old capital, and I met him by chance on the sea yesterday and chatted happily. During the conversation, he asked about the life of my friends and gradually moved on to (Doctor of Quality Studies); I did not know what it meant in a hurry, and after a moment of contemplation, I suddenly understood and laughed together for a long time.

(Doctor of Quality Studies) graduated from the University of Berlin in Germany. After returning to China, he immediately responded to the invitation of the ×× Academy in Beiping and served as a (Philosophy) professor; but on his name card, he wrote in large characters: (Doctor of Quality Studies). His peers were surprised by the novel title and asked him in their spare time: (The name you signed must be (Doctor of Geology). Did the printer accidentally omit the word (Earth) when it was printed)? He said: (No, no! What I study is not the structure of the earth's crust, but the principles of the universe. This kind of theory has a fixed name in European and American academic circles, how can there be any omission)? The questioner then realized that what he called (Quality Studies) was actually a mistake for (Philosophy): simply because (Quality) and (Philosophy) are homophones, the doctor was too broad-minded, which led to (confusing Li with Zhang), casting a big mistake. So he explained the meaning of the words in detail and corrected his mistakes; and the doctor was able to accept the advice and resolutely abandoned it, and never used it again. However, those name cards of his kind, which were scattered in the social field, were numerous, and it seemed as difficult to recover as spilled water; so the grand name of (Doctor of Quality Studies) was popularized.

It is now heard that the doctor has given up his educational career, hiding in the city, (long sleeves are good at dancing), and his reputation is growing. I wonder if, in his spare time, he can look back on the past and remember this old story of (Spring Bright)?

Our magazine will start publishing Mr. Zhang Henshui's new novel (*Little Western Paradise*) from the 20th. Please pay attention!

Supplement of Shen Bao, This City

Talking

From Foreign Countries to China 259

— Jiang Ming

When I was in elementary school, a Chinese expatriate who had returned from America told me that "there are no beggars in foreign countries because the government prohibits them." So, in my heart, I began to fantasize about what kind of "heavenly kingdom" this "foreign country" was, and even thought about going to that "heavenly kingdom" to enjoy life a little. Later, another Chinese expatriate who had returned from Luzon told me that "beggars are forbidden in foreign countries, but they can change their method of begging. Most of them hold a large handful of pencils and ask passersby for money. If you give them a few cents, they will give you a pencil as a sign of gratitude." Then I understood that the so-called "no beggars in foreign countries" was actually such a trick!

In the Shanghai concessions, beggars are similarly prohibited. Prison vans running through the streets picking up beggars is a common sight. But they can't catch them all. As soon as they leave the gates of the Municipal Council, they can only go back to begging. So, some time ago, they used freight cars to carry beggars to the Zhabei area to disperse them, not allowing them to return to the concessions. Naturally, the concessions are places with special powers, so we have nothing to say.

However, now, "(The Tianjin Social Bureau Massively Arrests Beggars)" (Shen Bao, 9th) but they also cannot catch them all. "Within two days, one branch alone arrested over 400 people. There are still over 20,000 people who wander the concessions making a living by begging." Seeing such a huge number will make your heart cold. If the "Tianjin Social Bureau" completely "captures" them all, the almshouses will definitely be unable to accommodate them, so what will they do with them then?

What is worth noting is "making a living as a beggar," which is truly both serious and humorous. Begging has also become a profession. It's truly laughable to say, but this is a serious problem. There are social reasons for its existence: when the rural economy collapses and urban unemployment is rampant, begging becomes a profession. If we were to tally up all the beggars in the country, the number would be staggering, probably at least one-fifth of the national population. To make so many beggars no longer exist in society, we must fundamentally transform society. Simply "catching" and "expelling" them like the concession authorities is definitely ineffective.

At the Wharf 260

— Jie Sun

After Uncle Cheng's banquet, all the luggage was moved, and Sister Yin staggered in. Today is a free day for the Buddha-worshipping festival. The room was dark and crowded with people seeing us off; some were seeing off Sister Yin, and some were seeing me off. The noise and shouts of the porters carrying luggage, and the usual farewell words, formed a very harsh sound. Hua, though a maid, was no less sorrowful than me! Her slightly gazing eyes and messy temples will be deeply remembered by me in the future!

The red glow of the setting sun shone on the lacquered red walls. I tearfully said goodbye to my aunts; and boarded the car with my brother and relatives and friends, speeding towards the noisy wharf. The chaotic feelings of parting made me feel uneasy!

The wharf was piled with a crowd of travelers, some returning home in glory, some wandering in destitution, some seeing off their loved ones for a thousand miles, and some leaving their parents far behind. These various kinds of travelers, with their different emotions of sorrow and joy, were naturally a mixture of sorrow and joy. Small boats weaved back and forth on the green waves like shuttles. I finally left my relatives and friends who were seeing me off, and left in a small boat! The fluttering skirt and waving handkerchief gradually blurred in my eyes! Before me was a green, shimmering expanse of gentle waves!

The small boat gradually approached the large ship. Thick smoke, like black clouds, poured rapidly from the ship's smokestack. We held onto the tall ladder, stepped on it cautiously, and carried our luggage into a rather delicate cabin. Ah, this will accompany me on my voyage for more than ten days!

My brother instructed Sister Yin many things, and Sister Yin's father also instructed her many things, probably meaning to teach her to take care of me. At this time, shaking hands with them and saying goodbye, the chaos in my heart cannot be described in words! The wailing whistle urged them to go back.

Leaning blankly against the iron railing, my eyes filled with hot tears almost rolled down! However, I finally tried my best to hold back! Because in the presence of so many eyes, I didn't want to show such weakness. The distant figure of my brother and the small boat slowly swayed towards the shore, my eyes full of hot tears, hold back, hold back!…

The whistle blew a long cry, and the green mountains, green trees, buildings, and houses on both sides retreated backwards. The ship suddenly started moving. The dazzling red light shone on the buildings, and the trees all turned red. Proudly, it seemed to be saying to me: "You child, go ahead! (To the barbaric foreign land,) don't be nostalgic anymore!"

I was filled with endless regret! My precious childhood vanished in the arms of this "(barbaric foreign land)!"

Now, now I want to return, return, with a heart full of longing, returning to my motherland!!!

The poetic coconut breeze and banana rain, and the, and the sunset reflected, the glittering waves of the Mekong River, from now on, from now on I can only savor you in my dreams!

The Little Braid 261

— Huai Ying

His name is Yang Dake, but the classmates all call him "Little Braid."

On the back of his left head, he wears a long braid. Is that the reason why the classmates gave him this nickname?

Yes, there is really no reason for a twelve-year-old boy like him to keep a braid. When asked about it, he said it was his mother's idea.

"Can't you shave it off yourself?"

If someone else asked him this question, he would think that they were teasing him again, but the one asking this question was me, his teacher, so he had to answer me seriously. He said:

"Mom won't let me shave it off. Mom says this is fulfilling some vow. I don't want to keep it either."

That's right, from the moment someone called him by his nickname, his face would turn red, as if he was a little embarrassed. I knew that he also hated this braid, but because I couldn't guess the reason, I asked like this. So, he is restricted by his mother, no, he is affected by the superstitious mentality under the old social system.

The child is not lacking in intelligence. He can answer and do all his homework, and he also writes a good hand. To be honest, my writing as a teacher is really not as good as his. He can also do everything in games, like kicking a leather ball. It's just that when someone grabs his braid, he looks like a child who has done something wrong and been discovered by an adult, silently hiding in a less crowded place.

He is often late, in fact, it can be said that he is late every day. The time he is late is always half an hour. When he comes, he quietly opens the classroom door, bows to me, and then walks to his seat. The other students then shift their gaze from the books to him.

Because of this, I was very unhappy and had severely punished him, making him stand, making him recite, making him wipe the glass, and even making him sweep the floor. I am a teacher, so I can't help but set an example for other students, which is also meant to warn the others through one person. It's strange, no matter how I punish him, he accepts it silently, not crying, not shouting, and not resisting. However, if you ask him the reason, he won't say it to the death, as if there is something difficult about it. Once, I hit his palms hard, and both pairs of hands were red and swollen, because he couldn't say the reason for being late, but he was late every day! His right hand and left hand were swollen in the same way, so it was not easy to hold the pen in the next calligraphy class.

"You are a cruel teacher!"

Seeing his situation, I regretted it very much. If it wasn't in front of a group of students, I really wanted to run up to him, grab both hands, and kiss them heavily a few times to atone for my sins.

Not only is he often late, but his hands and clothes are also often stained with a layer of rust. I feel that this is related to his being late, so I try to find out, but still, when I ask him what his family does for a living and who they are, he still doesn't answer me. My investigation gets no results.

One Sunday, the tin pot I was using somehow leaked a hole. If it wasn't repaired, it would simply become waste. I decided to find a tin pot shop to repair it.

Our school doesn't have errand boys, so as a teacher, if I want to drink boiled water, I have to make it myself. Naturally, I have to fix the pot myself. Humph, unexpectedly, the tin pot shop I found was opened by Little Braid's mother. He was banging on the tin sheet with a wooden stick. Looking at me, his face turned red, and then he took the pot over and told his mother who I was.

His mother, in addition to asking me to pay more attention to teaching her child, also asked me to forgive him for being half an hour late every day, because that half hour was his working

Page 20

time. Only then did I know the reason why Little Braid was late every day. I also heard a lot about his family's plight from his mother. This made me feel even more guilty about punishing him in the past.

"Little Braid, you are a good child, you are a poor child, I was wrong to blame you." On the way back to school, I repeated this to myself, while staring blankly at the repaired tin pot.

The Dried-Up Little River 262

— Wang Ci

"Green light, white light,

Sun-killing the old clam."

Sanlin'er stood on the grass, it was when the sun had just set. The eastern sky emitted a light like a Japanese flag – which farmers believe is a symbol of tomorrow's drought and heat – in Sanlin'er's mind, it was as if the heavens were calling him to sing a nursery rhyme, tilting his face, pouting his mouth, and vigorously:

"Green light!

White light!

Tomorrow in the Lu Riverbank, a big old clam will be sun-killed!"

Singing, happiness turned into a smile on his face, chasing a pair of big flowered chickens beside him.

The big flowered chickens were chased by Sanlin'er around the bend, rushing to the edge of the water bridge. Sanlin'er chased after them tremblingly, chasing the big flowered chickens to the point where they had nowhere to go:

Clap! Clap! Clap! Clap!

A pair of big flowered chickens had already rushed to the little river there.

The little river was no longer like a river, without a drop of water. In the dry yellow waterweed piles, there were three or four dead fish lying upside down with their bellies white; only in the lowest places was there a small ditch less than two inches wide, and the mud was still a bit soft and moist.

A pair of big flowered chickens jumped and walked on the riverbed, occasionally finding one or two deeper and wider ditches full of moisture and pecking to filter some water to drink, but they jumped away immediately.

Sanlin'er lived by the water bridge, no longer chasing after them, staring at the dry riverbed, and cried:

"Mom! Mom! Sanlin'er wants to eat dinner! Sanlin'er is so hungry!"

I don't know where the person Sanlin'er called Mom was. Sanlin'er cried so much, shouted so much; but there was no shadow.

A pitifully dried-up little river was still in front of Sanlin'er.

Sanlin'er knew that Mom went out in the daylight, to pedal a waterwheel more than half a mile away from where Sanlin'er was standing now; yesterday when Mom came back, it was almost dark, and Sanlin'er was also standing here, crying, seeing Mom coming, he threw his whole body on her, and Mom picked him up and kissed his cheek:

"Sanlin'er, good baby, why are you standing here crying?"

"Sanlin'er is hungry."

"Oh, oh, baby!!"

Mom pointed her lips towards the little river;

"The shallower the water in the river, the later Mom comes back; if it doesn't rain again tomorrow, Mom will come back even later! Baby, good baby, be patient!"

Sanlin'er listened very clearly, seeing Mom's eyes filled with tears, he felt bad and started crying again.

"Sanlin'er, good baby -" Mom really sobbed: "If the water in the river is always dry, Mom will never have food for you…"

The dried-up little river touched Sanlin'er's impression from yesterday: "If the water in the river is always dry, Mom will never have food for you!" Wasn't the little river dry today? Sanlin'er had no food to eat, Sanlin'er was hungry.

The sky slowly darkened.

On Selling Manuscripts 263

— Jun

Selling manuscripts and writing articles seem to be one and the same at first glance, and it seems impossible to distinguish any difference. In fact, it is not so, the two are very different. Selling manuscripts is one thing, and writing articles is another. Those who write articles generally do not regard writing as a specialized occupation, in other words, they do not make a living by writing, but treat it as a side business, a pastime, or an occasional fit of inspiration, writing something at will. The purpose is not necessarily to earn income from manuscripts, but often to vent the depression in their hearts for a while, or to entrust hidden thoughts to words, or to put their spirit into old chapters. Although the motivations may be different, they are all used to relieve emotions and entertain the eyes. This at least preserves a kind of selfless realm and a kind of intoxicated realm for the author. They write when they are happy, and they stop when they are not happy. Articles and life are separated from each other, so articles are somewhat of a spiritual respite and pleasure for them. As for selling manuscripts, it is completely different. The so-called selling manuscripts, obviously speaking, is to make a living solely by writing, turning articles into a specialized occupation. It closely connects manuscripts and life into a two-in-one relationship.

In this world, no matter what kind of event, if it is something that cannot be separated from one's life until old age, and even something that one is unwilling to do but still has to force oneself to do, then no matter how interesting it is, the original interest will inevitably gradually disappear with the passage of time, and one will gradually become tired of it. Why is writing alone an exception? Moreover, it is easier to feel tired and bored than anything else. At this time, the unique interest of articles disappears. Only those who are immersed in it can truly experience that taste. Once one relies solely on selling manuscripts to make a living, one can no longer have the casual attitude of expressing one's heart's content with a pen, but instead, it always contains the meaning of various struggles in life. Manuscripts are equivalent to life, and all the material resources, even the smallest details, must be produced from the tip of a pen. Life is like a green-faced, sharp-toothed demon, like a sharp leather whip, tightly whipping you, forcing you to move forward. For the sake of life, you cannot help but write, and you have to write even if you grit your teeth.

The pressure of solid reality, so they have to write because they are poor, so they desperately write, but sometimes the poorer they are, the less they can write, but they still have to desperately write, so they have to desperately create crudely and coarsely. For the sake of life, they have to do this, because if they stop writing, they will starve to death.

However, the individual's spiritual accumulation is very limited, not like a mountain spring that flows endlessly, and even a mine will eventually be completely exhausted. Not to mention humans? Therefore, for the sake of the amount of manuscript fees, they have to plan on this, and often in order to get some harvest, they try to lengthen the manuscript as much as possible and add some wasteful content.

When it comes to this, they are no longer writing articles, but have become craftsmen. Speaking of it, in this day and age, manuscripts are paid by the word, and articles are so worthless that there is nothing more to add. It is really a most tragic thing for writers to unfortunately want to warm their stomachs with their pens. Moreover, there is a risk of literary inspiration drying up, but the supply of life is endless. People are not made of iron, nor are they like machines that can continue to run by adding oil. Once Jiang Yan's talent is exhausted, but the manuscript still has to be written, then one has to rack one's brains and squeeze it out forcefully. Therefore, those who haggle over the words and sentences in manuscripts may not be of the highest quality, but they are also worthy of sighing.

Kept Woman 264

— Qing

What I expected to happen really happened without a doubt: she hasn't come for several days, which proves that the situation itself has undergone rapid changes. I had guessed long ago that she must be selling her only asset – her body – to another man again. In the middle of this month, she came to bother me almost every day, and every night in the dim early morning when the dance hall was over, she always quietly pushed open the door and came in. She turned on the light and woke me up from my sweet sleep.

Looking at her sitting on the edge of the bed, she smiled at me wantonly. Then, she simply leaned her upper body on the quilt and smiled again. At this time, I really felt a little angry. She shouldn't disturb my sweet sleep so absurdly, but on the other hand, I was dominated by a kind of seductive magic. The bright light shone on her face, and the rouge powder was unusually messy. But in that drowsy and tired state, it set off an even more unusual and moving coquettishness.

After she left, I thought of such a prostitute-like woman who lives a night-blooming life every day, and every night in that dark green place, on the melody of jazz music, she plays a charming and enchanting role, letting many strange men hold her in their arms and teasing and mocking her.

Love is gilded, using gold rings to buy temporary pleasure.

I met her in such a place, a commodity-like urban woman!

She would easily become intimate with me, and naturally, she would fall in love with someone else just as easily. I was very clear about it. I would never be infatuated enough to demand long-term possession of her. Moreover, almost every time she left, she never forgot about money, which made me feel cold all over when I thought about it.

It's just a pity that these kinds of women haven't recognized themselves, they look down on chastity as if they were looking down on a piece of paper, and they casually offer their bodies for men to trample on. As long as they can satisfy their material desires, they use their youth to live a luxurious and shameless life, a dissolute life. However, the period of youth, which serves as the decoration of life, is ultimately short and limited. When the time of fallen flowers has passed, it will be too late to regret it, right?

Now her behavior is exactly that of this kind of decadent urban woman. She is accelerating the destruction of her own life. She is sending herself to the edge of the grave step by step. This month of entanglement has really made me feel extremely disgusted with all women. Not just her, but now that she's gone, it really feels like shedding a whole body of debt and being relaxed.

Fool (6) 267

— Lin Bin

Like wildfire, the news spread into the wide gate of a building, reaching the ears of the village chief who was enjoying his opium, making him take a few less puffs. He immediately ordered the local constable to notify the heads of each household to expel this pair of demons creating poisonous germs, for the sake of the village's morals, the reputation of the Auspicious Temple, and for his, the village chief's, dignity. That day, Pockface was sent back to her parents' home, and Fool was banished from the village.

Two weeks later, I went to my uncle's house in Xiufa Village, thirty li away, on business. My uncle's gate was crowded with people, feet upon feet, heads pressed against heads, every eye fixed on the central hall inside, as if watching an absorbing illusion. Loud shouts echoed from the central hall, mixed with miserable and piercing cries, reminding me of the myth of the ox-headed demons of the Yama's palace brutally beating the wicked of three lifetimes.

Curious, I desperately squeezed up the stone steps of the gate, through the wide courtyard also packed with people, and to the front of the central hall. Suddenly, I felt a wave of dizziness, a pang of heartache, and a blur in my vision, as if I had truly entered Yama's palace.

Hanging from the right beam of the central hall was a half-naked body with large bones and thin muscles, hands tied behind, legs kicking frantically in the air. A brute-like man was vigorously whipping the half-dead, half-alive naked body with a red-wood thorn whip. Countless small holes oozed crimson blood, weaving a blurry web of blood. I focused my gaze on the face of the protagonist of this tragedy, and it turned out to be that Fool farmhand who had been banished from the village.

(He's a fool! Why?) I unconsciously said.

(Of course. Would someone who isn't crazy do such a thing? Would he offend a girl from such a family?) said one of the onlookers.

(But why exactly?) I seized the opportunity to ask.

(Haha... Miss Yan Xiufeng's grandmother, in the outhouse,) another said in a low voice, as if afraid someone would hear.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special Issue

The Original Creator of Hollywood's Only Soviet Star, Anna Sten (Part 2) 268

— Ming

This was a crucial moment for Anna's future success or failure. At that time, she would never have imagined that she would become a world-famous superstar, let alone that America would invite her.

Frank knew that if she didn't have a role in that film, she would be sent back to her country: undoubtedly, she would fail from then on. But he was unwilling for her to end up like that; he had to find a way to save her. Finally, he confessed to the company that he would pay Anna's salary during filming, and only then did the company agree to let her play the lead role in the film.

So, on the one hand, she worked hard to learn with the guidance of good teachers; on the other hand, she listened to Frank's advice and began to pay attention to her clothing. Under Frank's discerning eyes, she corrected many clumsy postures. In his sensitive ears, she corrected countless incorrect grammar. In just a few months, she transformed a rustic girl into a young lady born in a wealthy family.

As a result, she performed extremely well in the film. The film was a success, and Anna Sten also achieved tremendous personal success. From then on, her position was solidified, and the title of star was added to her name.

Did her efforts change her fate, and did her success change her person? No, it can be said that it did not change at all; she was still the same. Moreover, her success made her afraid. Whenever she met someone even slightly important, she would always ask Frank: (Did I say something wrong? Was my behavior correct?)

Frank built two houses in Germany. Originally, he only needed one for himself, but the German government wanted landowners to build more houses because the tax on vacant land was particularly heavy, so he built two and rented one to Anna. They became neighbors. Frank's wife had died long ago, and Anna often came to visit him and his little girl.

One day, Anna, dressed exceptionally beautifully, ran into his house and exclaimed: (I'm moving!) When Frank heard her words, his heart stopped beating. He gripped her hands tightly, as if afraid she would run away, and asked in a trembling voice: (Where are you moving to?) She said: (I'm moving into your house to live with you; I'm tired of paying rent, and I like this house too!) In the autumn of 1930, they got married.

Their wedding did not add to or subtract from their love. Later, when Goldwyn took Anna to America, Frank resigned from his job and followed her to America. The two of them were always together and never separated. Frank said that movies were his life, and Anna's success was his only wish.

This is a story about Anna Sten that Frank had never told anyone before. (The End)

Movie Reviews

Review of (A Couple's Mirror) 269

— Hu Yue

His Man is Mine Shown in Shanghai

(A Couple's Mirror) is a film depicting a love triangle.

A couple who have been married for five years experience a minor emotional entanglement when the man's old flame returns to their town. Eventually, the man's old flame marries someone else, and the couple reconciles.

There is a typical happy ending, a clichéd and well-worn romance, and ordinary and vulgar techniques.

(A Couple's Mirror) does not offer us anything particularly fresh; it is just like any other superficial love film, depicting the messy love affairs of young masters and misses.

(A Couple's Mirror) is similar to "Husband and Wife of Grievances", both narrating the trivial daily lives of the bourgeoisie in modern society.

Here, humorous and lighthearted dialogue amuses gentlemen and ladies, and brisk techniques give gentlemen and ladies entertainment and satisfaction. In this respect, the screenwriter has fulfilled his duty.

However, behind the laughter and satisfaction, how much ugliness is concealed, and how much cruel imagery is prettified.

Audience Opinions

My Review of (Woman) 270

— Huang Yingdai

(Woman) is undoubtedly a successful work among domestic films, I admit. First of all, the script is certainly conscious, depicting everything that three women with different personalities experience on their life journeys. In today's Chinese society, it is truly difficult for women to find a way out. But women cannot sell their souls just because it is difficult to find a way out, nor can they think that marriage is necessarily a solution.

(Woman) has clearly told us that most women, after having children, shift their love for their husbands to their children; and it is at this time that men's feelings towards women become indifferent, and they go off to love someone else. How wrong this is!

(Woman) also clearly indicates to us that since (September 18th Incident), the four northeastern provinces have been lost, and the lost territory has not yet been recovered. But the young people who have lost their souls, like Xiao Ting, have long forgotten this unprecedented national humiliation, and are immersed in dance halls day and night.

(Woman) is warning young people not to live in a drunken dream.

(Woman) not only takes social issues as its center but also contains educational significance, guiding those young men and women in society who are crying out not to go astray.

The director also knows how to use the camera effectively. Although there are many interjections, the audience does not find them annoying. The disputes in the women's dormitory, the villagers' rare and strange sights of seeing a young master bring a Shanghai miss back, and the scenes after (September 18th) of Shanghai city seen are discount banners, street riots, large factories, and large shops, often in bankruptcy. These external scenes can all be a portrayal of the real situation of Chinese cities and villages. Among the actors, Li Minghui does a good job in both the romantic period and the painful period, but when she was abandoned by Xiao Ting and Xiao Fen was burned to death, she never shed a single real tear, perhaps because she is not good at crying? Hu Ping's Jin Ling and Wang Yin's Xiao Ting both performed well.

Xiao Ting is such a frivolous young man, and in the end, he can only stroke the corpse and cry in vain. Regarding this point, it doesn't seem enough to please the audience, I think.

My Review of (Woman) 271

— Yong Sen

(Woman) does not solve the women's problem, nor does it indicate a way out for women.

However, there is a good inspiration given to the audience, which is to say: (Women) should be (good wives and mothers) after marrying their husbands, and should not (rely on their husbands). He narrates the life of Liang Yufen after marriage - waking up late, gambling, and the final encounter - economic hardship, being abandoned by her husband, burning her daughter to death... to awaken this generation of women in modern society, which is more powerful than writing directly. This is the cleverness of the playwright.

(Woman) has already received many praises, but I think there are several points that should be discussed, and it is not nitpicking.

First, Wang Yifang's studying is of course unwilling to do things that (sell the soul), and wants to extricate herself and seek progress. Unexpectedly, she was expelled from school; because of (having been a dancer, which hinders the school's ethos). Perhaps the playwright inserted this to speak out against the Nanjing song queen Wang Yurong; then, it should not be depicted that she specializes in applying makeup and being late for class at school, showing that her habits have not changed.

Second, whether Liang Yufen and others are university students or middle school students? However, judging from the level of chemistry, they are only middle school students. If it is a university course, it is too superficial!

Third, when Hong Xiaoting is (broke), why doesn't he go back to ask his mother for help? Didn't his mother subsidize him with three hundred yuan before he lost his job?

Fourth, when Liang Yufen is in poverty, she sends letters to many classmates to find work. Among them, one or two written forms should be added - Liang Yufen asks Jin Ling to find a job, or Jin Ling helps - because they are closer, and perhaps it will be smoother for the development of the story! I think.

In addition, the scenery is still good, the photography is slightly inferior to (Fisherman's Song), and although the subtitles are vigilant, they are not concise, even a sentence has more than twenty characters, and there are also typos such as one (will eventually do it for you), etc. (The rest is omitted)

Mistaking a Stranger for Husband in the Theater 272

— Shu Wen

Helen Twelvetrees once went to see a movie with her husband in a small suburban movie theater. It was so crowded that they had to sit separately. The movie was gradually getting to the main feature. During the most tense, exciting, and thrilling scenes, Helen was eating a bag of candy. She suddenly thought of her husband, so she handed the bag of candy to a man in the next seat. The man didn't say anything, just slowly pushed the bag away. After a while, Helen handed the bag of candy over again. However, the same thing happened again.

No matter what, she couldn't stand it anymore. So she questioned him why he was doing this. While saying this, she glared at him very angrily. Oh dear! This look was wrong. That person was not her husband!

Then she remembered. She was sitting separately from him, and they were far apart. Since discovering this, she was extremely embarrassed. She wanted to change seats, but there was no second seat to be found. She had no choice but to stop watching the movie, run out, sit in the car, and wait until the theater was over and her husband came out. Afterwards, her husband knew about it and laughed non-stop. Even now, Helen often tells others about this joke.

(Beautiful Heart) Returns to Original Title 273

(Beautiful Heart of Changbai Mountains), directed by Xu Xinfu, starring Hu Die, Gu Meijun, Wang Zhengxin, etc., was once renamed (Beautiful Heart), but now it has returned to its original title and is determined to be (Beautiful Heart of Changbai Mountains). The film depicts the difficult and arduous struggle of the Volunteer Army against the enemy, which is very profound and moving, and will probably be seen by the audience after the autumn cool.

Laurel's wrist was handcuffed to a detective named Flanagan. At that time, Eddie was coming out with Kai, looking angry. Welsh saw Eddie and greeted him. Laurel also stopped. Home
